	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">2006 Lebanon War</h1>

		<div id="contentSub"></div>

</p>

<li>The <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Army">Lebanese Army</a> is introduced into South Lebanon and <a href="/wiki/UNIFIL" class="mw-redirect" title="UNIFIL">UNIFIL</a> deployments reinforced</li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="background-color:#C3D6EF;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">Belligerents</th></tr><tr><td style="width:50%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;">

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Final_day_of_the_war_sees_Katyusha_rockets_in_Haifa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Final_day_of_the_war_sees_Katyusha_rockets_in_Haifa.jpg/220px-Final_day_of_the_war_sees_Katyusha_rockets_in_Haifa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Final_day_of_the_war_sees_Katyusha_rockets_in_Haifa.jpg/330px-Final_day_of_the_war_sees_Katyusha_rockets_in_Haifa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Final_day_of_the_war_sees_Katyusha_rockets_in_Haifa.jpg/440px-Final_day_of_the_war_sees_Katyusha_rockets_in_Haifa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1958" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Final_day_of_the_war_sees_Katyusha_rockets_in_Haifa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Smoke over <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>, Israel, after a rocket launched by <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> hit the city near Bnei-Zion hospital</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>2006 Lebanon War</b>, also called the <b>2006 Israel–Hezbollah War</b><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and known in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> as the <b>July War</b><sup id="cite_ref-DailyStarTimeline_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyStarTimeline-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">حرب تموز</span>&#8206;, <i>Ḥarb <a href="/wiki/Tammuz_(Hebrew_month)#Other_uses" title="Tammuz (Hebrew month)">Tammūz</a></i>) and in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> as the <b>Second Lebanon War</b> (<a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>: <span lang="he" dir="rtl">מלחמת לבנון השנייה</span>&#8206;, <i>Milhemet Levanon HaShniya</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> was a 34-day <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">military conflict</a> in Lebanon, Northern Israel and the <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">Golan Heights</a>. The principal parties were <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> paramilitary forces and the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> (IDF). The conflict started on 12 July 2006, and continued until a United Nations-brokered <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire" title="Ceasefire">ceasefire</a> went into effect in the morning on 14 August 2006, though it formally ended on 8 September 2006 when Israel lifted its naval <a href="/wiki/Blockade" title="Blockade">blockade</a> of Lebanon. Due to unprecedented Iranian military support to Hezbollah before and during the war, some consider it the first round of the <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_proxy_conflict" title="Iran–Israel proxy conflict">Iran–Israel proxy conflict</a>, rather than a continuation of the <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="Arab–Israeli conflict">Arab–Israeli conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-zisser_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zisser-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The conflict was precipitated by the <a href="/wiki/2006_Hezbollah_cross-border_raid" title="2006 Hezbollah cross-border raid">2006 Hezbollah cross-border raid</a>. On 12 July 2006, Hezbollah fighters fired <a href="/wiki/List_of_artillery#Rockets" title="List of artillery">rockets</a> at Israeli border towns as a diversion for an <a href="/wiki/Anti-tank_missile" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-tank missile">anti-tank missile</a> attack on two armored <a href="/wiki/Humvee" title="Humvee">Humvees</a> patrolling the Israeli side of the border fence.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_iht_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_iht-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The ambush left three soldiers dead. Two Israeli soldiers were abducted and taken by Hezbollah to Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_iht_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_iht-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Five more were killed in Lebanon, in a failed rescue attempt. Hezbollah demanded the release of Lebanese prisoners held by Israel in exchange for the release of the abducted soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Israel refused and responded with <a href="/wiki/Airstrike" title="Airstrike">airstrikes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a> fire on targets in Lebanon. Israel attacked both Hezbollah military targets and Lebanese civilian infrastructure, including Beirut's <a href="/wiki/Beirut_Rafic_Hariri_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Beirut Rafic Hariri International Airport">Rafic Hariri International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The IDF launched a ground invasion of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Lebanon" title="Southern Lebanon">Southern Lebanon</a>. Israel also imposed an air and naval <a href="/wiki/Blockade" title="Blockade">blockade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Hezbollah then launched more rockets into northern Israel and engaged the IDF in <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a> from hardened positions.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The conflict is believed to have killed between 1,191 and 1,300 Lebanese people,<sup id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lebanon_2006_pp._3-6_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebanon_2006_pp._3-6-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and 165 Israelis.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> It severely damaged Lebanese civil infrastructure, and displaced approximately one million Lebanese<sup id="cite_ref-hrc_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrc-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and 300,000–500,000 Israelis.<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_casualties_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa_casualties-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC:_Middle_East_crisis:_Facts_and_Figures_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_Middle_East_crisis:_Facts_and_Figures-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USA_Today:_Israel_says_it_will_relinquish_positions_to_Lebanese_army_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA_Today:_Israel_says_it_will_relinquish_positions_to_Lebanese_army-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 August 2006, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> unanimously approved <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1701" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1701">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1701</a> (UNSCR 1701) in an effort to end the hostilities. The resolution, which was approved by both the Lebanese and Israeli governments the following days, called for disarmament of Hezbollah, for withdrawal of the IDF from Lebanon, and for the deployment of the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Armed_Forces" title="Lebanese Armed Forces">Lebanese Armed Forces</a> and an enlarged <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Force_in_Lebanon" title="United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon">United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon</a> (UNIFIL) in the south. UNIFIL was given an expanded mandate, including the ability to use force to ensure that their area of operations was not used for hostile activities, and to resist attempts by force to prevent them from discharging their duties.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The Lebanese Army began deploying in Southern Lebanon on 17 August 2006. The blockade was lifted on 8 September 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On 1 October 2006, most Israeli troops withdrew from Lebanon, although the last of the troops continued to occupy the border-straddling village of <a href="/wiki/Ghajar" title="Ghajar">Ghajar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn.com_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In the time since the enactment of UNSCR 1701 both the Lebanese government and UNIFIL have stated that they will not disarm Hezbollah.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The remains of the two captured soldiers, whose fates were unknown, were returned to Israel on 16 July 2008 as part of a <a href="/wiki/2008_Israel%E2%80%93Hezbollah_prisoner_exchange" title="2008 Israel–Hezbollah prisoner exchange">prisoner exchange</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Lebanese_conflict" title="Israeli–Lebanese conflict">Israeli–Lebanese conflict</a></div>
<p>Cross-border attacks from <a href="/wiki/Southern_Lebanon" title="Southern Lebanon">southern Lebanon</a> into Israel by the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">Palestine Liberation Organization</a> (PLO) dated as far back as 1968, and followed the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a>; the area became a significant base for attacks following the arrival of the PLO leadership and its <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a> brigade following their 1971 <a href="/wiki/Black_September_in_Jordan" class="mw-redirect" title="Black September in Jordan">expulsion from Jordan</a>. Starting about this time, increasing <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Lebanon" title="Demographics of Lebanon">demographic tensions</a> related to the Lebanese <a href="/wiki/National_Pact" title="National Pact">National Pact</a>, which had divided governmental powers among religious groups throughout the country 30 years previously, began running high and led in part to the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War" title="Lebanese Civil War">Lebanese Civil War</a> (1975–1990).
</p><p>Concurrently, Syria began a <a href="/wiki/Syrian_occupation_of_Lebanon" title="Syrian occupation of Lebanon">29-year military occupation</a> in 1976. Israel's <a href="/wiki/Operation_Litani" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Litani">1978 invasion of Lebanon</a> failed to stem the Palestinian attacks in the long run, but <a href="/wiki/1982_Lebanon_War" title="1982 Lebanon War">Israel invaded Lebanon</a> again in 1982 and forcibly expelled the PLO.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Israel withdrew to a <a href="/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_southern_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli occupation of southern Lebanon">borderland buffer zone</a> in southern Lebanon, held with the aid of proxy militants in the <a href="/wiki/South_Lebanon_Army" title="South Lebanon Army">South Lebanon Army</a> (SLA).<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta:_Arab–Israeli_Conflict_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta:_Arab–Israeli_Conflict-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The invasion also led to the conception of a new <a href="/wiki/Shi%27a" class="mw-redirect" title="Shi&#39;a">Shi'a</a> <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">militant group</a>, which in 1985, established itself politically under the name <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>, and declared an armed struggle to end the <a href="/wiki/South_Lebanon_conflict_(1985%E2%80%932000)" title="South Lebanon conflict (1985–2000)">Israeli occupation</a> of Lebanese territory.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encarta:_Hassan_Nasrallah_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta:_Hassan_Nasrallah-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> When the Lebanese Civil War ended and other warring factions agreed to disarm, both Hezbollah and the SLA refused. Ten years later, Israel withdrew from South Lebanon to the UN-designated and internationally recognized <a href="/wiki/Blue_Line_(Lebanon)" title="Blue Line (Lebanon)">Blue Line</a> border in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The withdrawal also led to the immediate collapse of the SLA, and Hezbollah quickly took control of the area. Later, citing continued Israeli control of the <a href="/wiki/Shebaa_farms" title="Shebaa farms">Shebaa farms</a> region and the <a href="/wiki/Internment" title="Internment">internment</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_prisoners_in_Israel" title="Lebanese prisoners in Israel">Lebanese prisoners in Israel</a>, Hezbollah intensified its cross-border attacks, and used the tactic of seizing soldiers from Israel as leverage for a <a href="/wiki/Israeli_MIA_prisoner_exchanges" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli MIA prisoner exchanges">prisoner exchange</a> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Institute_for_Palestinian_Studies_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Institute_for_Palestinian_Studies-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boston_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boston-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> All told, from summer 2000, after the Israeli withdrawal, until summer 2006, Hezbollah conducted approximately 200 attacks on Israel – most of them artillery fire, some raids and some via proxies inside Israel. In these attacks, including the attack that precipitated the Israeli response that developed into the war, 31 Israelis were killed and 104 were wounded.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In August 2006, in an article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Hersh" title="Seymour Hersh">Seymour Hersh</a> claimed that the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> gave the green light for the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli government">Israeli government</a> to execute an attack on Hezbollah in Lebanon. Supposedly, communication between the Israeli government and the US government about this came as early as two months in advance of the capture of two Israeli soldiers and the killing of eight others by Hezbollah prior to the conflict in July 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The US government denied these claims.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Conal Urquhart in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, the Winograd Committee leaked a testimony from Israeli Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Olmert" title="Ehud Olmert">Ehud Olmert</a> suggesting that Olmert "had been preparing for such a war at least four months before the official <i>casus belli</i>: the capture by Hezbollah of two Israeli soldiers from a border post on 12 July 2006."<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abduction_efforts_in_the_year_prior_to_conflict">Abduction efforts in the year prior to conflict</span></h3>
<p>In June 2005, an <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> (IDF) paratroop unit operating near the <a href="/wiki/Shebaa_Farms" class="mw-redirect" title="Shebaa Farms">Shebaa Farms</a> engaged three Lebanese it identified as Hezbollah special force members, killing one. Videotapes recovered by the paratroopers contained footage of the three recording detailed accounts of the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Harel_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harel-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over the following 12 months, Hezbollah made three unsuccessful attempts to abduct Israeli soldiers. On 21 November 2005, a number of Hezbollah special forces attempted to attack an Israeli outpost in <a href="/wiki/Ghajar" title="Ghajar">Ghajar</a>, a village straddling the border between Lebanon and the <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">Golan Heights</a>. The outpost had been deserted following an intelligence warning, and three of the Hezbollah militants were killed when Israeli sniper David Markovich shot a <a href="/wiki/Rocket-propelled_grenade" title="Rocket-propelled grenade">rocket-propelled grenade</a> they were carrying, causing it to explode. From his sniper position, Markovich shot and killed a fourth gunman shortly thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-Harel_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harel-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline_of_the_war">Timeline of the war</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="Timeline of the 2006 Lebanon War">Timeline of the 2006 Lebanon War</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_operations_of_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="Military operations of the 2006 Lebanon War">Military operations of the 2006 Lebanon War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_military_operations_in_the_2006_Lebanon_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of military operations in the 2006 Lebanon War">Timeline of military operations in the 2006 Lebanon War</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hezbollah_cross-border_raid">Hezbollah cross-border raid</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_Hezbollah_cross-border_raid" title="2006 Hezbollah cross-border raid">2006 Hezbollah cross-border raid</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zarit_incident_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Zarit_incident_map.png/350px-Zarit_incident_map.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8a/Zarit_incident_map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="519" data-file-height="298" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zarit_incident_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/2006_Hezbollah_cross-border_raid" title="2006 Hezbollah cross-border raid">cross-border raid</a> map</div></div></div>
<p>At around 9&#160;AM local time on 12 July 2006, Hezbollah launched <a href="/wiki/Feint" title="Feint">diversionary</a> rocket attacks toward Israeli military positions near the coast and near the border village of <a href="/wiki/Zar%27it" title="Zar&#39;it">Zar'it</a><sup id="cite_ref-unreport_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unreport-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> as well as on the Israeli town of <a href="/wiki/Shlomi_(town)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shlomi (town)">Shlomi</a> and other villages.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Five civilians were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Six Israeli military positions were fired on, and the surveillance cameras knocked out.<sup id="cite_ref-Exit_Strategy_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exit_Strategy-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the same time, a Hezbollah ground contingent infiltrated the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Line_(Lebanon)" title="Blue Line (Lebanon)">border</a> into Israel through a "dead zone" in the border fence, hiding in an overgrown <a href="/wiki/Wadi" title="Wadi">wadi</a>. They attacked a patrol of two Israeli <a href="/wiki/Humvee" title="Humvee">Humvees</a> patrolling the border near Zar'it, using pre-positioned explosives and anti-tank missiles, killing three soldiers, injuring two, and capturing two soldiers (First Sergeant <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Goldwasser" title="Ehud Goldwasser">Ehud Goldwasser</a> and Sergeant First Class <a href="/wiki/Eldad_Regev" title="Eldad Regev">Eldad Regev</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-unreport_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unreport-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In response to the Hezbollah feint attacks, the IDF conducted a routine check of its positions and patrols, and found that contact with two jeeps was lost. A rescue force was immediately dispatched to the area, and confirmed that two soldiers were missing after 20 minutes. A <a href="/wiki/Merkava" title="Merkava">Merkava Mk III</a> tank, an <a href="/wiki/Armored_personnel_carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Armored personnel carrier">Armored personnel carrier</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopter</a> were immediately dispatched into Lebanon. The tank hit a large land mine, killing its crew of four. Another soldier was killed and two lightly injured by mortar fire as they attempted to recover the bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-unreport_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unreport-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Exit_Strategy_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exit_Strategy-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hezbollah named the attack "<a href="/wiki/2006_Hezbollah_cross-border_raid" title="2006 Hezbollah cross-border raid">Operation Truthful Promise</a>" after leader <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Nasrallah" title="Hassan Nasrallah">Hassan Nasrallah</a>'s public pledges over the prior year and a half to seize Israeli soldiers and swap them for <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_prisoners_in_Israel" title="Lebanese prisoners in Israel">four Lebanese held by Israel</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Samir_Kuntar" title="Samir Kuntar">Samir Kuntar</a> (<i>a Lebanese citizen captured during an attack in 1979, convicted of murdering civilians and a police officer</i>);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nasim_Nisr" title="Nasim Nisr">Nasim Nisr</a> (<i>an Israeli-Lebanese citizen whom Israel tried and convicted for spying</i>);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yahya_Skaf" title="Yahya Skaf">Yahya Skaf</a> (<i>a Lebanese citizen whom Hezbollah claims was arrested in Israel; Israel states that he was killed in action</i>);<sup id="cite_ref-nasrallah_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nasrallah-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ali_Faratan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ali Faratan (page does not exist)">Ali Faratan</a> (<i>another Lebanese citizen whom Hezbollah claimed to be held in Israel, believed to have been shot at sea.</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Nasrallah claimed that Israel had broken a previous deal to release these prisoners, and since diplomacy had failed, violence was the only remaining option.<sup id="cite_ref-nasrallah_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nasrallah-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Nasrallah declared that "no military operation will result in rescuing these prisoners... The only method, as I indicated, is that of indirect negotiations and a swap [of prisoners]".<sup id="cite_ref-nasrallah_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nasrallah-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israeli_response">Israeli response</span></h3>
<p>Israeli Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Olmert" title="Ehud Olmert">Ehud Olmert</a> described the seizure of the soldiers as an "act of war" by the sovereign state of Lebanon,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> stating that "Lebanon will bear the consequences of its actions"<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> and promising a "very painful and far-reaching response."<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Israel blamed the Lebanese government for the raid, as it was carried out from Lebanese territory.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Hezbollah had two ministers serving in the Lebanese cabinet at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-cnnceasefire_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnceasefire-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In response, Lebanese Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Fouad_Siniora" title="Fouad Siniora">Fouad Siniora</a> denied any knowledge of the raid and stated that he did not condone it.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lebanon2_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebanon2-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> An emergency meeting of the Lebanese government reaffirmed this position.<sup id="cite_ref-Lebanon1_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebanon1-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> attacked targets within Lebanon with artillery and airstrikes hours before the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Israel" title="Cabinet of Israel">Israeli Cabinet</a> met to discuss a response. The targets consisted of bridges and roads in Lebanon, which were hit to prevent Hezbollah from transporting the abductees. An Israeli airstrike also destroyed the runways of <a href="/wiki/Beirut_Rafic_Hariri_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Beirut Rafic Hariri International Airport">Beirut Rafic Hariri International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> 44 civilians were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-DailyStarTimeline_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyStarTimeline-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The Israeli Air Force also targeted Hezbollah's long range rocket and missile stockpiles destroying many of them on the ground in the first days of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-Avi_Issascharoff_2008_pp._179_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avi_Issascharoff_2008_pp._179-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-missilesfirstday_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-missilesfirstday-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Many of Hezbollah's longer-range rocket launchers were destroyed within the first hours of the Israeli attack.<sup id="cite_ref-Exit_Strategy_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exit_Strategy-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later that same day (12 July 2006), the Cabinet decided to authorize the Prime Minister, the Defense Minister and their deputies to pursue the plan which they had proposed for action within Lebanon. Prime Minister Olmert officially demanded that the Israel Defense Forces avoid civilian casualties whenever possible.<sup id="cite_ref-Prime_Minister&#39;s_Office:_Decision_#258_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prime_Minister&#39;s_Office:_Decision_#258-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Israel's <a href="/wiki/Ramatkal" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramatkal">chief of staff</a> <a href="/wiki/Dan_Halutz" title="Dan Halutz">Dan Halutz</a> said, "if the soldiers are not returned, we will turn Lebanon's clock back 20 years"<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_severe_response_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_severe_response-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> while the head of Israel's Northern Command <a href="/wiki/Udi_Adam" title="Udi Adam">Udi Adam</a> said, "this affair is between Israel and the state of Lebanon. Where to attack? Once it is inside Lebanon, everything is legitimate – not just southern Lebanon, not just the line of <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> posts."<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_severe_response_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_severe_response-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 12 July 2006, the Israeli Cabinet promised that Israel would "respond aggressively and harshly to those who carried out, and are responsible for, today's action".<sup id="cite_ref-communiqué_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-communiqué-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The Cabinet's communiqué stated, in part, that the "Lebanese Government [was] responsible for the action that originated on its soil."<sup id="cite_ref-communiqué_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-communiqué-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> A retired Israeli Army Colonel explained that the rationale behind the attack was to create a rift between the Lebanese population and Hezbollah supporters by exacting a heavy price from the elite in <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 July, the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Israel" title="Cabinet of Israel">Israeli Cabinet</a> released a communiqué explaining that, although Israel had engaged in military operations <i>within</i> Lebanon, its war was not against the Lebanese government. The communiqué stated: "Israel is not fighting Lebanon but the terrorist element there, led by Nasrallah and his cohorts, who have made Lebanon a hostage and created Syrian- and Iranian-sponsored terrorist enclaves of murder."<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When asked in August about the proportionality of the response, Prime Minister Olmert stated that the "war started not only by killing eight Israeli soldiers and abducting two but by shooting <a href="/wiki/Katyusha_rocket_launcher" title="Katyusha rocket launcher">Katyusha</a> and other rockets on the northern cities of Israel on that same morning. Indiscriminately." He added "no country in Europe would have responded in such a restrained manner as Israel did."<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israeli_air_and_artillery_attacks">Israeli air and artillery attacks</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dahiya_doctrine" title="Dahiya doctrine">Dahiya doctrine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haret_Hreik_Before_After_22_July_2006.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/76/Haret_Hreik_Before_After_22_July_2006.png/220px-Haret_Hreik_Before_After_22_July_2006.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/76/Haret_Hreik_Before_After_22_July_2006.png 1.5x" data-file-width="252" data-file-height="353" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haret_Hreik_Before_After_22_July_2006.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite photographs of the <a href="/wiki/Haret_Hreik" title="Haret Hreik">Haret Hreik</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>-dominated neighborhood <a href="/wiki/Dahieh" title="Dahieh">Dahieh</a> district of southern Beirut, Lebanon, before and after 22 July 2006. The neighborhood is home to Hezbollah's headquarters. <i>See also high resolution photographs <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://maps.google.com/maps?f=q&amp;hl=en&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;t=k&amp;om=1&amp;ll=33.853346,35.508993&amp;spn=0.010425,0.021415">before</a> and <cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070821013412/http://www.digitalglobe.com/images/qb/beirut_harat_july22_2006_dgwm.jpg">"after"</a>. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.digitalglobe.com/images/qb/beirut_harat_july22_2006_dgwm.jpg">the original</a> on 21 August 2007.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=after&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.digitalglobe.com%2Fimages%2Fqb%2Fbeirut_harat_july22_2006_dgwm.jpg&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3A2006+Lebanon+War" .id-lock-subscription a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-subscription code.cs1-code{color:inherit;background:inherit;border:inherit;padding:inherit}.mw-parser-output .cs1-hidden-error{display:none;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-right{padding-right:0.2em}</style></i></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombed_commercial_centre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Bombed_commercial_centre.jpg/220px-Bombed_commercial_centre.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Bombed_commercial_centre.jpg/330px-Bombed_commercial_centre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Bombed_commercial_centre.jpg/440px-Bombed_commercial_centre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombed_commercial_centre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A building in <a href="/wiki/Ghazieh" title="Ghazieh">Ghazieh</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Sidon" title="Sidon">Sidon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghaziyeh_airstrikes" title="Ghaziyeh airstrikes">bombed</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force" title="Israeli Air Force">Israeli Air Force</a> (IAF)</div></div></div>
<p>During the first day of the war the Israeli Air Force, artillery and navy conducted more than 100 attacks mainly against Hezbollah bases in south Lebanon, among them the regional headquarters in Ya'tar. Five bridges across the Litani and Zahrani rivers were also destroyed, reportedly to prevent Hezbollah from transferring the abducted soldiers to the north.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Attacks from land, sea and air continued in the following days. Among the targets hit were the Hezbollah headquarters in the southern suburbs of Beirut as well as the offices and homes of the leadership, the compounds of <a href="/wiki/Al-Manar" title="Al-Manar">al-Manar</a> TV station and <a href="/wiki/Al-Nour" title="Al-Nour">al-Nour</a> radio station, and the runways and fuel depots of the <a href="/wiki/Rafic_Hariri_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rafic Hariri International Airport">Rafic Hariri International Airport</a> in Beirut. Also targeted were Hezbollah bases, weapons depots and outposts as well as bridges, roads and petrol stations in south Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> 44 civilians were killed throughout the day.<sup id="cite_ref-DailyStarTimeline_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyStarTimeline-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was later reported that the Israel Air Force after midnight, 13 July, attacked and destroyed 59 stationary medium range <a href="/wiki/Fajr" class="mw-redirect" title="Fajr">Fajr</a> rocket launchers positioned throughout southern Lebanon. <b><a href="/wiki/Operation_Density" title="Operation Density">Operation Density</a></b> allegedly only took 34 minutes to carry out but was the result of six years of intelligence gathering and planning. Between half and two-thirds of Hezbollah medium range rocket capability was estimated by the IDF to have been wiped out. According to Israeli journalists Amos Harel and Avi Issacharoff the operation was "Israel's most impressive military action" and a "devastating blow for Hezbollah". In the coming days IAF allegedly also attacked and destroyed a large proportion of Hezbollah's long range <a href="/wiki/Zelzal-2" title="Zelzal-2">Zelzal-2</a> missiles.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>"All the long-range rockets have been destroyed," Chief of Staff Halutz allegedly told the Israeli government, "we've won the war."<sup id="cite_ref-Times_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to military analyst <a href="/wiki/William_Arkin" title="William Arkin">William Arkin</a> there is "little evidence" that the Israeli Air Force even attempted, much less succeeded in, wiping out the medium and long range rocket capability in the first days of the war. He dismissed the whole claim as an "absurdity" and a "tale".<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Benjamin Lambeth, however, insisted that it was far-fetched to suggest that the "authoritative Israeli leadership pronouncements" were not based on facts. He admitted however that there was "persistent uncertainty" surrounding the "few known facts and figures" concerning the alleged attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Cordesman" title="Anthony Cordesman">Anthony Cordesman</a> believed that IAF probably destroyed most long and medium range missiles in the first two days of the war but acknowledged that these claims "have never been validated or described in detail."<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hezbollah long remained silent on this episode of the war. On the sixth anniversary of the Lebanon war Hezbollah chairman Hassan Nasrallah claimed that Hezbollah had known that the Israelis were collecting information on the rocket platforms and launchers and managed to move them without being detected. Most of the locations attacked by the Israeli air force were therefore empty.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>American officials claimed that the Israelis overstated the effectiveness of the air war against Hezbollah and cited the failure to hit any of the Hezbollah leaders in spite of dropping 23 tons of bombs on its alleged headquarters bunker.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Al-Manar TV station only went dark for two minutes after the strike before it was back into the air. The TV station was bombed 15 times during the war but never faltered after the first hiccup.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Locations_bombed_Aug13_no_fact_box.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Locations_bombed_Aug13_no_fact_box.jpg/220px-Locations_bombed_Aug13_no_fact_box.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Locations_bombed_Aug13_no_fact_box.jpg/330px-Locations_bombed_Aug13_no_fact_box.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Locations_bombed_Aug13_no_fact_box.jpg/440px-Locations_bombed_Aug13_no_fact_box.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1093" data-file-height="1639" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Locations_bombed_Aug13_no_fact_box.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Areas in Lebanon targeted by Israeli bombing, 12 July to 13 August 2006</div></div></div>
<p>During the war the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force" title="Israeli Air Force">Israeli Air Force</a> flew 11,897 combat missions, which was more than the number of sorties during the <a href="/wiki/1973_October_War" class="mw-redirect" title="1973 October War">1973 October War</a> (11,223) and almost double the number during the 1982 <a href="/wiki/1982_Lebanon_War" title="1982 Lebanon War">First Lebanon War</a> (6,052).<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Artillery_Corps_(Israel)" title="Artillery Corps (Israel)">Israeli artillery</a> fired 170,000 shells, more than twice the number fired in the 1973 October War.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> A senior officer in the IDF Armored Corps told <i><a href="/wiki/Haaretz" title="Haaretz">Haaretz</a></i> that he would be surprised if it turned out that even five Hezbollah fighters had been killed by the 170,000 shells fired.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Navy" title="Israeli Navy">Israeli Navy</a> fired 2,500 shells.<sup id="cite_ref-jdw230806_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jdw230806-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The combined effect of the massive air and artillery bombardment on Hezbollah capacity to fire short-range Katyusha rockets on northern Israel was very meager. According to the findings of the post-war military investigations the IDF shelling succeeded only in destroying about 100 out of 12,000 Katyusha launchers. The massive fire led to a severe shortage of ammunition towards the end of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northern command had prepared a list before the war on potential Hezbollah targets, identified by the Israeli intelligence, to be struck in case of renewed hostilities. By the fourth day of the war the IDF ran out of targets, as all the 83 targets on the list had already been hit.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> A high-ranking IDF officer told reporters off the record that the Israeli Chief of Staff Dan Halutz had ordered the air force to destroy ten 12-story buildings in the Southern suburbs of Beirut for every rocket that fell on Haifa. The statement was denied by the IDF spokesperson.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Large parts of the Lebanese civilian infrastructure, however, were destroyed, including <span style="white-space:nowrap">400&#160;miles&#160;(640&#160;km)</span> of roads, 73 bridges, and 31 other targets such as Beirut's <a href="/wiki/Beirut_Rafic_Hariri_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Beirut Rafic Hariri International Airport">Rafic Hariri International Airport</a>, ports, water and sewage treatment plants, electrical facilities, 25 fuel stations, 900 commercial structures, up to 350 schools and two hospitals, and 15,000 homes. Some 130,000 more homes were damaged.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hezbollah_rocket_attacks">Hezbollah rocket attacks</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2006crisis_lebanon_israel.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/2006crisis_lebanon_israel.png/220px-2006crisis_lebanon_israel.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/2006crisis_lebanon_israel.png/330px-2006crisis_lebanon_israel.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/2006crisis_lebanon_israel.png/440px-2006crisis_lebanon_israel.png 2x" data-file-width="637" data-file-height="592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2006crisis_lebanon_israel.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing some of the localities in Israel and the Golan Heights hit by rockets fired from Lebanese soil as of Monday 7 August.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KiryatShmona_Rocket_Damage.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/KiryatShmona_Rocket_Damage.JPG/170px-KiryatShmona_Rocket_Damage.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/KiryatShmona_Rocket_Damage.JPG/255px-KiryatShmona_Rocket_Damage.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/KiryatShmona_Rocket_Damage.JPG/340px-KiryatShmona_Rocket_Damage.JPG 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KiryatShmona_Rocket_Damage.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Structural damage of a residential building in <a href="/wiki/Kiryat_Shmona" title="Kiryat Shmona">Kiryat Shmona</a> after being hit by a rocket</div></div></div>
<p>On 16 July, eight employees of the Israel Railways were killed by direct rocket hits on the Haifa train depot.<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_casualties_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa_casualties-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Hezbollah leader Hassan Nasrallah defended the attacks, saying that Hezbollah initially had aimed its rockets on "military sites only". But since Israel, he said, had systematically bombed civilian targets he felt that Hezbollah had no choice but to answer in kind and target Israeli cities.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The attack on the Haifa depot was not the first civilian target to be hit by Hezbollah. Civilians in the border communities were hurt in the initial cover fire on IDF positions for the cross-border raid. Two Israeli civilians were killed in an attack near the air force base at <a href="/wiki/Mount_Meron" title="Mount Meron">Mount Meron</a> on July, 14. Since Hezbollah rockets were not very accurate it is unclear whether civilians were intentionally targeted in these attacks. After the attack on Haifa, however, Hezbollah made no attempt to cover this fact. According to a Human Rights Watch study civilian Israeli targets were mentioned four times as often in official Hezbollah war time communiques as was military targets.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hezbollah TV station al-Manar warned both in Arabic and Hebrew specific Israeli communities for future rocket attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Similarly Hezbollah sent text messages to warn Israeli residents to evacuate their homes to avoid being targeted by rocket attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Israel published an alleged range card for upgraded Grad rocket launcher placed outside the village of Shihin in the Western sector of South Lebanon, issued by the Artillery Department of the elite Nasr Unit of Hezbollah. This list included 91 targets, 56 of whom were civilian and 27 were IDF posts or bases. The military targets had three-digit reference numbers while civilian targets had double-digit numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the war, the <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah_rocket_force" class="mw-redirect" title="Hezbollah rocket force">Hezbollah rocket force</a> fired between 3,970 and 4,228 rockets at a rate of more than 100 per day, unprecedented since the <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War" title="Iran–Iraq War">Iran–Iraq War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mideast_War,_by_the_numbers_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mideast_War,_by_the_numbers-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RCANI_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCANI-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> About 95% of these were 122&#160;mm (4.8&#160;in) <a href="/wiki/Katyusha_rocket_launcher" title="Katyusha rocket launcher">Katyusha</a> <a href="/wiki/Rocket_artillery" title="Rocket artillery">artillery rockets</a>, which carried warheads up to 30&#160;kg (66&#160;<a href="/wiki/Pound_(mass)" title="Pound (mass)">lb</a>) and had a range of up to 30&#160;km (19&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-RCANI_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCANI-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> An estimated 23% of these rockets hit cities and built-up areas across northern Israel, while the remainder hit open areas.<sup id="cite_ref-jdw230806_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jdw230806-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mideast_War,_by_the_numbers_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mideast_War,_by_the_numbers-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RCANI_136-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCANI-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cities hit were <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hadera" title="Hadera">Hadera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nazareth" title="Nazareth">Nazareth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiberias" title="Tiberias">Tiberias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nahariya" title="Nahariya">Nahariya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Safed" title="Safed">Safed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaghur" title="Shaghur">Shaghur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afula" title="Afula">Afula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiryat_Shmona" title="Kiryat Shmona">Kiryat Shmona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beit_She%27an" title="Beit She&#39;an">Beit She'an</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karmiel" title="Karmiel">Karmiel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ma%27alot-Tarshiha" title="Ma&#39;alot-Tarshiha">Ma'alot-Tarshiha</a>, as well as dozens of towns, <a href="/wiki/Kibbutz" title="Kibbutz">kibbutzim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moshav" title="Moshav">moshavim</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arab_citizens_of_Israel#Druze" title="Arab citizens of Israel">Druze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arab_citizens_of_Israel" title="Arab citizens of Israel">Israeli-Arab</a> villages. The northern <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> was also hit.<sup id="cite_ref-jdw230806_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jdw230806-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mideast_War,_by_the_numbers_135-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mideast_War,_by_the_numbers-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RCANI_136-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCANI-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTmap_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTmap-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Israeli_Defense_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli Defense Minister">Israeli Defense Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Amir_Peretz" title="Amir Peretz">Amir Peretz</a> ordered commanders to prepare civil defense plans. One million Israelis had to stay near or in bomb shelters or security rooms, with some 250,000 civilians evacuating the north and relocating to other areas of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-RCANI_136-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCANI-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the high number of Lebanese civilian casualties in the <a href="/wiki/Qana_airstrike" title="Qana airstrike">Qana airstrike</a>, Israel announced a unilateral freeze in its air attacks on Lebanon. Hezbollah then halted its own rocket attacks on Israel. When Israel resumed its air attacks on Lebanon, Hezbollah followed suit and recommenced rocket attacks on Israeli targets.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hezbollah rocket attacks also targeted and succeeded in hitting military targets in Israel. The Israeli military censorship was, however, very strict and explicitly forbade Israel-based media from reporting such incidents. The war time instruction to media stated that "The Military Censor will not approve reports on missile hits at IDF bases and/or strategic facilities."<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> A notable exception was the rocket attack 6 August, on a company of IDF reservists assembling in the border community of <a href="/wiki/Kfar_Giladi" title="Kfar Giladi">Kfar Giladi</a>, which killed 12 soldiers and wounded several others. Initially Israel did not confirm that the victims were military but eventually relented.
</p><p>6 August, two elderly Arab women in Haifa were killed, and an Arab man was mortally wounded, by Hezbollah rocket fire.<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_casualties_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa_casualties-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The day after Hezbollah leader Nasrallah appealed to Haifa's Arab community to leave the city so as not be hurt.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the initial Israeli response, Hezbollah declared an all-out military alert. Hezbollah was estimated to have 13,000 missiles at the beginning of the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Israeli newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Haaretz" title="Haaretz">Haaretz</a></i> described Hezbollah as a trained, skilled, well-organized, and highly motivated infantry that was equipped with the cream of modern weaponry from the arsenals of <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, Iran, Russia, and China.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Hezbollah's satellite TV station <a href="/wiki/Al-Manar" title="Al-Manar">Al-Manar</a> reported that the attacks had included a <a href="/wiki/Fajr-3_(rocket)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fajr-3 (rocket)">Fajr-3</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Ra%27ad_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Ra&#39;ad 1">Ra'ad 1</a>, both liquid-fuel missiles developed by Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-globalsecurity_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalsecurity-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Manar_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manar-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_war">Ground war</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hezbollah_Secret_Bunker_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hezbollah_Secret_Bunker_%281%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hezbollah_Secret_Bunker_%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hezbollah_Secret_Bunker_%281%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hezbollah_Secret_Bunker_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hezbollah_Secret_Bunker_%281%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hezbollah_Secret_Bunker_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1330" data-file-height="868" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hezbollah_Secret_Bunker_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Israeli soldier tosses a grenade into a Hezbollah bunker</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D9N_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/D9N_02.jpg/220px-D9N_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="94" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/D9N_02.jpg/330px-D9N_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/D9N_02.jpg/440px-D9N_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="564" data-file-height="242" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D9N_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/IDF_Caterpillar_D9" title="IDF Caterpillar D9">IDF Caterpillar D9</a>N <a href="/wiki/Armored_bulldozer" title="Armored bulldozer">armored bulldozers</a> destroy a Hezbollah bunker.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hezbolladefenseslebanon.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2f/Hezbolladefenseslebanon.png/220px-Hezbolladefenseslebanon.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2f/Hezbolladefenseslebanon.png/330px-Hezbolladefenseslebanon.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2f/Hezbolladefenseslebanon.png/440px-Hezbolladefenseslebanon.png 2x" data-file-width="886" data-file-height="497" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hezbolladefenseslebanon.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>War map, "Hezbollah Defensive System in Southern Lebanon", 2006</div></div></div>
<p>Hezbollah engaged in <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a> with IDF ground forces, fighting from well-fortified positions, often in urban areas, and attacking with small, well-armed units. Hezbollah fighters were highly trained, and were equipped with flak jackets, <a href="/wiki/Night_vision_device" class="mw-redirect" title="Night vision device">night-vision goggles</a>, communications equipment, and sometimes with Israeli uniforms and equipment. An Israeli soldier who participated in the war said that Hezbollah fighters were "nothing like <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> or the Palestinians. They are trained and highly qualified. All of us were kind of surprised."<sup id="cite_ref-disciplined_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disciplined-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During engagements with the IDF, Hezbollah concentrated on inflicting losses on the IDF, believing an unwillingness to absorb steady losses to be Israel's strategic weakness.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hezbollah countered IDF armor through the use of sophisticated Iranian-made <a href="/wiki/Anti-tank_guided_missile" title="Anti-tank guided missile">anti-tank guided missiles</a> (ATGMs). According to Merkava tank program administration, 52 <a href="/wiki/Merkava" title="Merkava">Merkava</a> <a href="/wiki/Main_battle_tank" title="Main battle tank">main battle tanks</a> were damaged (45 of them by different kinds of ATGM), missiles penetrated 22 tanks, but only 5 tanks were destroyed, one of them by an <a href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device" title="Improvised explosive device">improvised explosive device</a> (IED). The Merkava tanks that were penetrated were predominantly <a href="/wiki/Merkava_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Merkava II">Mark II</a> and Mark III models, but five <a href="/wiki/Merkava_Mk._IV" class="mw-redirect" title="Merkava Mk. IV">Mark IVs</a> were also penetrated. All but two of these tanks were rebuilt and returned to service.<sup id="cite_ref-jdw230806_122-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jdw230806-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The IDF declared itself satisfied with the Merkava Mark IV's performance during the war. Hezbollah caused additional casualties using ATGMs to collapse buildings onto Israeli troops sheltering inside.<sup id="cite_ref-jdw230806_122-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jdw230806-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> As a result, IDF units did not linger in any one area for an extended period of time.<sup id="cite_ref-disciplined_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disciplined-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Hezbollah fighters often used <a href="/wiki/Tunnel_warfare" title="Tunnel warfare">tunnels</a> to emerge quickly, fire an anti-tank missile, and then disappear again.<sup id="cite_ref-disciplined_150-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disciplined-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 July a force from the <a href="/wiki/Maglan" title="Maglan">Maglan special forces unit</a> seized a fortified Hezbollah dugout adjacent to the Shaked post; two IDF soldiers and five Hezbollah operatives were killed in the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Position_of_Lebanon">Position of Lebanon</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Position_of_Lebanon_in_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="Position of Lebanon in the 2006 Lebanon War">Position of Lebanon in the 2006 Lebanon War</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Siniora_Plan" title="Siniora Plan">Siniora Plan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Lebanon" title="Foreign relations of Lebanon">Foreign relations of Lebanon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fouad_Sinora.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Fouad_Sinora.jpg/170px-Fouad_Sinora.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="277" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Fouad_Sinora.jpg/255px-Fouad_Sinora.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Fouad_Sinora.jpg/340px-Fouad_Sinora.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="2447" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fouad_Sinora.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lebanon's Prime Minister Fouad Siniora</div></div></div>
<p>While the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli government">Israeli government</a> initially held the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese government">Lebanese government</a> responsible for the Hezbollah attacks due to Lebanon's failure to implement <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1559" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1559">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1559</a> and disarm Hezbollah, Lebanon disavowed the raids, stating that the government of Lebanon did not condone them, and pointing out that Israel had a long history of disregarding UN resolutions.<sup id="cite_ref-Lebanon2_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebanon2-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In interviews, <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_President" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese President">Lebanese President</a> <a href="/wiki/Emile_Lahoud" class="mw-redirect" title="Emile Lahoud">Emile Lahoud</a> criticized Israel's attacks and was supportive of Hezbollah, noting <a href="/wiki/South_Lebanon_conflict_(1985%E2%80%932000)" title="South Lebanon conflict (1985–2000)">Hezbollah's role in ending Israel's previous occupation of southern Lebanon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CBC:_Lebanese_president_gives_full_backing_to_Hezbollah._153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBC:_Lebanese_president_gives_full_backing_to_Hezbollah.-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC:_UN_diplomacy_may_not_end_conflict:_Lebanese_President_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC:_UN_diplomacy_may_not_end_conflict:_Lebanese_President-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> On 12 July 2006, <a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Broadcasting Service">PBS</a> interviewed the Lebanese ambassador <a href="/wiki/Farid_Abboud" title="Farid Abboud">Farid Abboud</a> to the United States and his Israeli counterpart. The interview discussed Hezbollah's connection to the Lebanese government.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Israel never <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_war" title="Declaration of war">declared war</a> on Lebanon,<sup id="cite_ref-MFA:_Behind_the_Headlines:_UN_Security_Council_Resolution_1701_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFA:_Behind_the_Headlines:_UN_Security_Council_Resolution_1701-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC:_More_About_the_History_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC:_More_About_the_History-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> and said it only attacked Lebanese governmental institutions which it suspected of being used by Hezbollah.<sup id="cite_ref-MFA:_Behind_the_Headlines:_Israel&#39;s_counter_terrorist_campaign_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFA:_Behind_the_Headlines:_Israel&#39;s_counter_terrorist_campaign-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The Lebanese government played a role in shaping the conflict. On 14 July 2006, the office of Lebanese Prime Minister Fouad Siniora issued a statement that called on US President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> to exert all his efforts on Israel to stop its attacks in Lebanon and reach a comprehensive ceasefire.<sup id="cite_ref-Washington_Post:_Bush_Declines_to_Call_for_Israeli_Cease-fire_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_Post:_Bush_Declines_to_Call_for_Israeli_Cease-fire-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> In a televised speech the next day, Siniora called for "an immediate ceasefire backed by the United Nations."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>A US-French draft resolution that was influenced by the Lebanese <a href="/wiki/Siniora_Plan" title="Siniora Plan">Siniora Plan</a> and which contained provisions for Israeli withdrawal, military actions, and mutual prisoner release was rejected by the US and Israel. Many Lebanese accused the US government of stalling the ceasefire resolution and of support of Israel's attacks. In a poll conducted two weeks into the conflict, only 8% of the respondents felt that the US would support Lebanon, while 87% supported Hezbollah's fight against Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Qana_airstrike" title="Qana airstrike">attack on Qana</a>, Siniora snubbed US Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> by cancelling a meeting with her and thanked Hezbollah for its "sacrifices for the independence and sovereignty of Lebanon."<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the war, the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Armed_Forces" title="Lebanese Armed Forces">Lebanese Armed Forces</a> did not engage in direct hostilities, but threatened retaliation if IDF troops pushed too far northward into Lebanon. In several instances, Lebanese troops fired anti-aircraft weapons at Israeli aircraft and attempted to disrupt landing operations.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> During the first days of the war, Lebanese Defense Minister Elias Murr said that "the Lebanese army will resist and defend the country. If there is an invasion of Lebanon, we are waiting for them." However, the Lebanese Army mostly stayed out of the fighting. According to a <i><a href="/wiki/Time_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Magazine">Time</a></i> editorial, "to have stood up to the advancing Israeli armored columns would have been suicidal."<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> On 7 August 2006, the 7-point plan was extended to include the deployment of 15,000 Lebanese Army troops to fill the void between an Israeli withdrawal and UNIFIL deployment.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceasefire">Ceasefire</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire_attempts_during_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="Ceasefire attempts during the 2006 Lebanon War">Ceasefire attempts during the 2006 Lebanon War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg/220px-Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg/330px-Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg/440px-Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="784" data-file-height="728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Israeli soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/Nahal_Brigade" title="Nahal Brigade">Nahal Brigade</a> leaving Lebanon</div></div></div>
<p>Terms for a ceasefire had been drawn and revised several times over the course of the conflict, yet successful agreement between the two sides took several weeks. Hezbollah maintained the desire for an unconditional ceasefire,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> while Israel insisted upon a conditional ceasefire, including the return of the two seized soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Lebanon frequently pleaded for the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> to call for an immediate, unconditional ceasefire between Israel and Hezbollah. <a href="/wiki/John_R._Bolton" class="mw-redirect" title="John R. Bolton">John Bolton</a> confirmed that the US and UK, with support from several Arab leaders, delayed the ceasefire process. Outsider efforts to interfere with a ceasefire only ended when it became apparent Hezbollah would not be easily defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 August 2006 the United Nations Security Council unanimously approved <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council_Resolution_1701" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council Resolution 1701">UN Security Council Resolution 1701</a>, in an effort to end the hostilities. It was accepted by the Lebanese government and Hezbollah on 12 August 2006, and by the Israeli government on 13 August 2006. The ceasefire took effect at 8:00&#160;AM (5:00&#160;AM GMT) on 14 August 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the ceasefire, the two Hezbollah members of cabinet said that their militia would not disarm south of the <a href="/wiki/Litani_River" title="Litani River">Litani River</a>, according to another senior member of the Lebanese cabinet,<sup id="cite_ref-cnnceasefire_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnceasefire-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> while a top Hezbollah official similarly denied any intention of disarming in the south. Israel said it would stop withdrawing from <a href="/wiki/Southern_Lebanon" title="Southern Lebanon">Southern Lebanon</a> if <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Armed_Forces" title="Lebanese Armed Forces">Lebanese troops</a> were not deployed there within a matter of days.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Techniques">Techniques</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cluster_and_phosphorus_munitions">Cluster and phosphorus munitions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Cluster_Munitions" title="Convention on Cluster Munitions">Convention on Cluster Munitions</a></div>
<p>Both sides used <a href="/wiki/Cluster_bombs#Lebanon,_1978,_1982_and_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Cluster bombs">cluster bombs</a> during the conflict. Israel fired 4.6&#160;million submunitions into dozens of towns and villages in southern Lebanon in 962 separate strikes, circa 90% within the final 72 hours of the war, when the conflict already had been largely resolved by UN Security Council Resolution 1701.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW_Flooding_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW_Flooding-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Entire towns were covered in cluster bombs. The unguided and imprecise rockets were fired from mobile rocket launching platforms. To compensate for the inaccuracy of the rockets, the areas were flooded with munitions.<sup id="cite_ref-Rappaport_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rappaport-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Israel claimed to have warned civilians prior to a strike, and that firing was limited to open areas or military targets inside urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Israel used advanced cluster munitions produced by <a href="/wiki/Israel_Military_Industries" class="mw-redirect" title="Israel Military Industries">Israel Military Industries</a>, and large numbers of older cluster bombs, some produced in the 1970s, purchased from aging American stockpiles. These were fired by <a href="/wiki/Multiple_rocket_launcher" title="Multiple rocket launcher">multiple rocket launchers</a>, 155mm artillery guns, and dropped by aircraft. As many as 1&#160;million submunitions failed to explode on impact, lingering as land mines that killed or maimed almost 200 people since the war ended.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2006_Lebanon_War&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, munitions were still causing casualties and being cleared by volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hezbollah fired 4,407 submunitions into civilian-populated areas of northern Israel in 113 separate strikes, using Chinese made <a href="/wiki/Type_81_(rocket_launcher)" title="Type 81 (rocket launcher)">Type-81</a> 122mm rockets, and Type-90 submunitions. These attacks killed one civilian and wounded twelve.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> "found that the IDF's use of cluster munitions was both indiscriminate and disproportionate, in violation of IHL, and in some locations possibly a war crime" because "the vast majority [were dropped] over the final three days when Israel knew a settlement was imminent."<sup id="cite_ref-HRW_Flooding_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW_Flooding-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> After the ceasefire, parts of southern Lebanon remained uninhabitable due to Israeli unexploded cluster bomblets.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also phosphorus shells were used by the IDF to attack civilian areas in Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> The shells were originally designed to generate a <a href="/wiki/Smoke_screen" title="Smoke screen">smoke screen</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Battlespace#From_&#39;Battlefield&#39;_to_&#39;Battlespace&#39;" title="Battlespace">battlefield</a> situation, but <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus#White_phosphorus_and_related_molecular_forms" title="Phosphorus">white phosphor</a> is also especially harmful to humans because its burning will continue inside the flesh. The shelling was investigated as a violation of <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Psychological_warfare">Psychological warfare</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Psychological_warfare" title="Psychological warfare">Psychological warfare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Information_warfare" title="Information warfare">Information warfare</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Disinformation" title="Disinformation">Disinformation</a></div>
<p>During the war, the IAF dropped 17,000 leaflets over Lebanon in 47 missions, and sent more than 700,000 computerized voice messages. Many of them contained caricatures of Hassan Nasrallah and Hezbollah leading Lebanon to ruin and making civilians suffer, showing them as puppets of Iran and Syria, and calling on civilians to help remove Hezbollah. Another leaflet addressing Hezbollah fighters told them that they were lied to by their leaders, that they were "sent like sheep to be butchered, lacking military training and without proper combat gear", that they could not hope to face "highly trained soldiers that fight to protect their homeland, their people, and their home", referring to them as "mercenaries" without the support of the Lebanese public, and urging them to run and save their lives. On 26 July, Israel dropped leaflets containing illustrations of nine tombstones with the name of a dead Hezbollah fighter on each one, in response to Nasrallah "deceiving" people on the amount of Hezbollah casualties. Another leaflet urged Hezbollah fighters to stop bleeding and fighting for Nasrallah, who sat safe in a bunker, to stop fighting against Lebanese national interests, and to return to their homes and families. On 11 August, Israel dropped leaflets accusing Hezbollah of hiding its "great losses", and containing the names of 90–100 Hezbollah fighters killed.
