Israeli technicians also hacked into <a href="/wiki/Al-Manar" title="Al-Manar">Al-Manar</a> and broadcast clips, criticizing Nasrallah, showing the bodies of Hezbollah fighters, footage from Israeli raids and airstrikes, and captured Hezbollah equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Casualties_and_damage">Casualties and damage</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Casualties_of_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="Casualties of the 2006 Lebanon War">Casualties of the 2006 Lebanon War</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lebanese_civilians_and_combatants">Lebanese civilians and combatants</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Lebanon_refugee.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/South_Lebanon_refugee.jpg/220px-South_Lebanon_refugee.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/South_Lebanon_refugee.jpg/330px-South_Lebanon_refugee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/South_Lebanon_refugee.jpg/440px-South_Lebanon_refugee.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Lebanon_refugee.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lebanese <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_persons" class="mw-redirect" title="Internally displaced persons">IDPs</a> in south Lebanon, 2006</div></div></div>
<p>The Lebanese civilian death toll is difficult to pinpoint as most published figures, including those released by the Lebanese government, do not distinguish between civilians and Hezbollah combatants.<sup id="cite_ref-apstats_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apstats-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Hezbollah fighters can be difficult to identify as many do not wear military uniforms.<sup id="cite_ref-apstats_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apstats-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> However, it has been widely reported that the majority of the Lebanese killed were civilians, and <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> estimated that 30% of Lebanese killed were children under the age of 13.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
The Lebanese top police office and the Lebanon Ministry of Health, citing hospitals, death certificates, local authorities, and eye witnesses, put the death toll at 1,123—37 soldiers and police officers, 894 identified victims, and 192 unidentified ones.<sup id="cite_ref-apstats_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apstats-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon_Higher_Relief_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lebanon Higher Relief Council (page does not exist)">Lebanon Higher Relief Council</a> (HRC) put the Lebanese death toll at 1,191,<sup id="cite_ref-hrc_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrc-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> citing the health ministry and police, as well as other state agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-apstats_33-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apstats-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> estimated the figure at 1,035.<sup id="cite_ref-apstats_33-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apstats-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In February 2007, the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> reported that at least 800 Lebanese had died during fighting,<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> and other articles have estimated the figure to be at least 850.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Encarta" title="Encarta">Encarta</a> states that <i>"estimates ... varied from about 850 to 1,200"</i> in its entry on Israel,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> while giving a figure of <i>"more than 1,200"</i> in its entry on Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> The Lebanon Higher Relief Council estimated the number of Lebanese injured to be 4,409,<sup id="cite_ref-hrc_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrc-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> 15% of whom were permanently disabled.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The death toll estimates do not include Lebanese killed since the end of fighting by <a href="/wiki/Land_mine" title="Land mine">land mines</a> or unexploded Israeli <a href="/wiki/Cluster_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Cluster bomb">cluster bombs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-apstats_33-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apstats-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Between the end of the war and November 2008, approximately 40 people were killed and over 270 injured by cluster bombs.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hezbollah_and_other_militias">Hezbollah and other militias</span></h3>
<p>During the war Hezbollah kept a firm lid on its casualties. Although it did announce casualty numbers in some of the clashes, the party did not publish a comprehensive estimate for the duration of the war. A tally made by <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> counted to 70 dead Hezbollah fighters officially acknowledged by party during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghattas_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghattas-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 6 August <i><a href="/wiki/Haaretz" title="Haaretz">Haaretz</a></i> reported the IDF placing the number of Hezbollah fighters killed at 400, but added that "armies fighting guerrilla forces tend to exaggerate the fatalities of the enemy".<sup id="cite_ref-NoComp_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NoComp-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Matt M. Matthews military historian at <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Combined_Arms_Center" title="United States Army Combined Arms Center">United States Army Combined Arms Center</a>, also described these figures as "highly exaggerated" because he asserts that Hezbollah suffered only 187 casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 4 August 2006 <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Telegraph" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily Telegraph">Daily Telegraph</a></i> article by <a href="/wiki/Con_Coughlin" title="Con Coughlin">Con Coughlin</a>, referring to estimates by Lebanese officials, said that up to 500 Hezbollah fighters had been killed and 1,500 wounded. According to the article, many of Hezbollah's wounded were secretly evacuated to hospitals in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> through the Al-Arissa Border Crossing. A later article by the <i>Daily Telegraph</i> said that funerals of fallen Hezbollah fighters were "staggered" and were interred without ceremony for re-burial later. Coughlin quoted a senior Lebanese security official as saying that "Hizbollah is desperate to conceal its casualties because it wants to give the impression that it is winning its war. People might reach a very different conclusion if they knew the true extent of Hizbollah's casualties." According to the article, Hezbollah's operational council had drawn up casualty lists to be sent to <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, as the Iranian government compensated the families of Hezbollah's dead, and that Hezbollah had pressured Lebanese newspapers that had obtained copies not to publish them.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/John_Keegan" title="John Keegan">John Keegan</a> wrote in an op-ed that "perhaps as many as 1,000" Hezbollah fighters were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Stratfor" title="Stratfor">Stratfor</a> report cited "sources in Lebanon" as estimating the Hezbollah death toll at "more than 700 fighters with many more to go",<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Intelligence analysts <a href="/wiki/Alastair_Crooke" title="Alastair Crooke">Alastair Crooke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Perry_(author)" title="Mark Perry (author)">Mark Perry</a> reported a few months after the war a total of 184 "Shiite martyr funerals" having been held in Lebanon since the war. They considered this number an indication of Hezbollah fatalities but warned that it could be revised upward in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>IDF Maj.-Gen. (res.) Yaakov Amidror said that IDF had identified the names of 440 members of Hezbollah who were killed in the war. Based on this number he estimated that the total amounted killed in the war to between 500 and 700.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Later, Israel claimed to have identified 532 dead Hezbollah fighters and estimated that an additional 200 were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Four months after the end of the war the deputy chairman of the Hezbollah Political Council <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mahmoud_Qomati&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mahmoud Qomati (page does not exist)">Mahmoud Qomati</a> substantially raised the official estimate of the number of Hezbollah fatalities. He now claimed that 250 fighters had been killed in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghattas_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghattas-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JP250_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JP250-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Israel meanwhile also backed down from its war-time estimates. Instead of the 800 Hezbollah fatalities said during the war, Israeli government spokesperson <a href="/wiki/Miri_Eisin" title="Miri Eisin">Miri Eisin</a> in December revised that estimate, saying, "We think that it's closer to 600."<sup id="cite_ref-JP250_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JP250-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Three years after the outbreak of war the Israel Ministry of Foreign Affairs published a summary of the war which concluded that over 600 Hezbollah fighters were killed in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-MFA09_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFA09-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hezbollah claimed that many of Hezbollah's dead were local village fighters rather than regulars. However, according to one analyst, who noted that general estimates place Hezbollah's losses at around 500–600 fighters out of a regular fighting force of 2,000, "this was mainly party propaganda attempting to put a brave face on what was by any measure a major blow to the resistance," and claimed that Hezbollah subsequently went on a recruitment drive to replace its losses.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Yedioth_Ahronoth" title="Yedioth Ahronoth">Yedioth Ahronoth</a></i> "Encyclopedia" of the Second Lebanon War, the main reason for the discrepancy between Lebanese and Israeli estimates of the number of Hezbollah fatalities during the war (700 and 300 respectively) was that the former included only Hezbollah <b>combatants</b> while the latter also included <b>civilian</b> members of Hezbollah.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> The NGO <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> argued that in 94 IDF air, artillery, and ground attacks during the war that claimed the lives of 561 persons, that only 51 of these were combatants and about half of them were women or children.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> HRW said it documented the identities of another 548 fatalities, bringing the total of identified Lebanese deaths in the war to 1109. It argued (as an extrapolation from those 94 attacks) that an estimated 250 of these were Hezbollah combatants and the remaining 860 were civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Amal_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Amal movement">Amal movement</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Shiite" class="mw-redirect" title="Shiite">Shiite</a> militia that fought alongside Hezbollah, suffered 17 dead. Armed elements of the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Communist_Party" title="Lebanese Communist Party">Lebanese Communist Party</a> suffered 12 dead. The <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Palestine_%E2%80%93_General_Command" title="Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine – General Command">Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine – General Command</a>, a Palestinian militia, lost two fighters in an Israeli air raid.<sup id="cite_ref-DailyStarTimeline_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyStarTimeline-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> There are also unconfirmed reports that a number of Iranian Revolutionary Guard soldiers were killed in the fighting.<sup id="cite_ref-nysun1_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nysun1-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ynetnews1_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ynetnews1-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aviationweek.com_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aviationweek.com-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> A statement issued by the Israel Ministry of Foreign Affairs after the war detailed what it termed "Iranian complicity" in the Lebanese crisis, which included training and supplying Hezbollah forces.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Although unnamed "diplomatic sources" had claimed the presence of "hundreds" of Revolutionary Guard soldiers during the conflict, Iran denied that any were present or killed.<sup id="cite_ref-nysun2_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nysun2-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hezbollah_commanders">Hezbollah commanders</span></h4>
<p>Hezbollah General-Secretary Hassan Nasrallah said in an interview with New TV August shortly after the war that between 10 and 12 Hezbollah commanders were killed in the war. None of the first or second levels of the leadership were harmed. Three commanders of the third level however were killed; an operations officer in the Bint Jbeil axis, a logistics officer and a third commander involved in the military side of the party. In addition three or four town commanders and four or five village commanders were killed in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nasrallah did not mention any names but some of these were subsequently identified. Squad leader Muhammad Dimashq (nome de guerre: Jawad Ayta) was shot 21 July, by an Israeli sniper in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Maroun_al-Ras" title="Battle of Maroun al-Ras">battle of Maroun ar-Ras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Two Hezbollah commanders were killed in an Israeli air strike in the Old City of Bint Jbeil July, 29. <a href="/wiki/Khalid_Bazzi" title="Khalid Bazzi">Khalid Bazzi</a> (nome de guerre: al-Hajj Qasim) was chief of operations in the Bint Jbeil area, including Maroun al-Ras, Aynata, Aytaroun and Bint Jbeil, while Muhammad Abu Ta'am was commander of the forces in the town itself. Both had taken part in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Hezbollah_cross-border_raid" title="2006 Hezbollah cross-border raid">abduction</a> of the two Israeli soldiers that had started the war.<sup id="cite_ref-EpicSafir_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EpicSafir-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> On the last day of the war, Muhammad Qansuh (nome de guerre: Sajid ad-Duwayr), a special force commander and Bazzi’s successor as Bint Jbeil commander, was killed in another air raid on Bint Jbeil.<sup id="cite_ref-SajidLeb_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SajidLeb-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SajidIsr_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SajidIsr-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> According to the IDF, he was in fact killed in an airstrike on the <a href="/wiki/Dahieh,_Beirut" class="mw-redirect" title="Dahieh, Beirut">Dahiya</a> district of Beirut.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two Hezbollah commanders were killed in battles around Wadi Hujeir/Wadi Sulouqi. Rani Adnan Bazzi died in hand-to-hand combat, together with seven of his men, in the strategic town of al-Ghandouriya, controlling the strategic wadi crossing. A further three fighters were wounded in the battle and one of them were taken prisoner by the IDF.<sup id="cite_ref-SafGhand_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SafGhand-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Commander Ali Mahmoud Salih (nome de guerre: Bilal) fought singlehandedly further up the wadi, firing ATGM rockets at the advancing Israeli tanks. In the end he was severely wounded by a drone strike and died some time later from his wounds.
<sup id="cite_ref-Al_Akhbar_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al_Akhbar-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lebanese_Armed_Forces">Lebanese Armed Forces</span></h3>
<p>Though rarely engaged in combat, 43 <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Armed_Forces" title="Lebanese Armed Forces">Lebanese soldiers</a> and policemen were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-DailyStarTimeline_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyStarTimeline-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israeli_civilians">Israeli civilians</span></h3>
<table class="infobox bordered">

<tbody><tr>
<td colspan="colnum" style="text-align:center;">Israeli civilians killed by Hezbollah rocket attacks, 12 July – 13 August 2006 (black)<br /> vs. the ethnic composition at the North of Israel (pink).<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_1a6be107b22a1c592a541673cfa35351"></map><img usemap="#timeline_1a6be107b22a1c592a541673cfa35351" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/1a6be107b22a1c592a541673cfa35351.png" /></div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Hezbollah rockets and mortars killed 44 Israeli civilians during the conflict, including a severely wounded Haifa resident who died from his wounds more than a year after the war. In addition four elderly died of heart attacks during rocket attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_casualty_details_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa_casualty_details-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> At least 19 of the 46 Israeli civilians killed by Hezbollah rockets and mortars were <a href="/wiki/Arab_citizens_of_Israel" title="Arab citizens of Israel">Israeli Arabs</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslims">Sunni Muslims</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-pmo-dp_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmo-dp-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ynet-dp_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ynet-dp-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> The last civilian victim was an Israeli-Arab man who died on 30 August 2007, from injuries sustained in a rocket attack on <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> In addition, 4,262 civilians were injured–33 seriously wounded, 68 moderately, 1,388 lightly, and 2,773 suffered from <a href="/wiki/Post-traumatic_stress_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-traumatic stress disorder">shock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anxiety" title="Anxiety">anxiety</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_casualties_61-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa_casualties-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> According to Human Rights Watch, "These bombs may have killed 'only' 43 civilians, but that says more about the availability of warning systems and bomb shelters throughout most of Northern Israel and the evacuation of more than 350,000 people than it does about Hezbollah's intentions."<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel_Defense_Forces">Israel Defense Forces</span></h3>
<p>A total of 121 <a href="/wiki/Israeli_casualties_of_war" title="Israeli casualties of war">IDF soldiers were killed</a> in the war, including the two soldiers who were seized in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Hezbollah_cross-border_raid" title="2006 Hezbollah cross-border raid">cross-border raid</a> that started the war. Their fates were not confirmed until their bodies were <a href="/wiki/2008_Israel%E2%80%93Hezbollah_prisoner_exchange" title="2008 Israel–Hezbollah prisoner exchange">exchanged for Lebanese prisoners in 2008</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mfa_casualties_61-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa_casualties-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mfa_casualty_details_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa_casualty_details-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Matériel losses in the Israeli Defense Forces accounted for 5<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> to 20<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> tanks depending in the source. 3 helicopters were lost to accidents and 1 to Hezbollah missile fire. 1 Fixed wing F-16 was lost during take off.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>  5 tanks were damaged beyond repair ('lasting vehicle kills'), 22 tanks received armor penetrations, and 52 tanks suffered some form of damage.<sup id="cite_ref-globes.co.il_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globes.co.il-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rolling_Thunder_2013_page_172_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Thunder_2013_page_172-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECordesmanSullivan2007&quot;Only_5–6_of_all_types_represented_a_lasting_vehicle_kill&quot;110_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECordesmanSullivan2007&quot;Only_5–6_of_all_types_represented_a_lasting_vehicle_kill&quot;110-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> other sources claim 20 main battle tanks destroyed (6 to mines, 14 to anti tanks guided missiles- all Merkava II,III or IV).<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 14 July, a Hezbollah operated <a href="/wiki/C-802" class="mw-redirect" title="C-802">C-802</a> anti-ship missile struck an Israeli Navy gunship killing 4 sailors and damaging the warship.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/INS_Hanit" title="INS Hanit">INS Hanit</a> was damaged on the waterline, under the aft superstructure<sup id="cite_ref-JP_ship_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JP_ship-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_missile_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_missile-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> by a missile (likely a Chinese-designed <a href="/wiki/C-802" class="mw-redirect" title="C-802">C-802</a><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>) fired by <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> that reportedly set the flight deck on fire and crippled the propulsion systems inside the hull.<sup id="cite_ref-defenceupdat_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-defenceupdat-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> However, INS <i>Hanit</i> stayed afloat, withdrew and made the rest of the journey back to <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Ashdod" title="Port of Ashdod">Ashdod port</a> for repairs under its own power.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Four crew members were killed during the attack: Staff Sergeant Tal Amgar, Corporal Shai Atas, Sergeant Yaniv Hershkovitz, and First Sergeant Dov Steinshuss.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UN_personnel">UN personnel</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_incidents_during_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="International incidents during the 2006 Lebanon War">International incidents during the 2006 Lebanon War</a></div>
<p>4 United Nations Military Observers were killed and several more wounded.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_and_archeological_damage">Environmental and archeological damage</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Jiyeh_power_station_oil_spill" class="mw-redirect" title="Jiyeh power station oil spill">Jiyeh power station oil spill</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jiyyeh_oil_spill_2006_NASA_ASTER.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Jiyyeh_oil_spill_2006_NASA_ASTER.jpg/170px-Jiyyeh_oil_spill_2006_NASA_ASTER.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Jiyyeh_oil_spill_2006_NASA_ASTER.jpg/255px-Jiyyeh_oil_spill_2006_NASA_ASTER.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Jiyyeh_oil_spill_2006_NASA_ASTER.jpg/340px-Jiyyeh_oil_spill_2006_NASA_ASTER.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jiyyeh_oil_spill_2006_NASA_ASTER.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Image from space showing Jiyyeh oil slick in darkest blue, picture centered on Beirut. The largest <a href="/wiki/Oil_spill" title="Oil spill">oil spill</a> in the history of the Mediterranean, it was caused by an <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force" title="Israeli Air Force">Israeli air strike</a> on <a href="/wiki/Jiyeh" class="mw-redirect" title="Jiyeh">Jiyeh</a> power station<sup id="cite_ref-seattlepi_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattlepi-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> 10 August 2006</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_4484_Birya_Forest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PikiWiki_Israel_4484_Birya_Forest.jpg/220px-PikiWiki_Israel_4484_Birya_Forest.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PikiWiki_Israel_4484_Birya_Forest.jpg/330px-PikiWiki_Israel_4484_Birya_Forest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/PikiWiki_Israel_4484_Birya_Forest.jpg/440px-PikiWiki_Israel_4484_Birya_Forest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_4484_Birya_Forest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A burnt forest in northern Israel caused by Hezbollah rockets</div></div></div>
<p>On 13 July 2006, and again on 15 July 2006, the Israeli Air Force bombed the <a href="/wiki/Jiyeh_power_station_oil_spill" class="mw-redirect" title="Jiyeh power station oil spill">Jiyeh power station</a>, 30&#160;km (19&#160;mi) south of Beirut, resulting in the largest ever oil spill in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-seattlepi_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattlepi-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> The plant's damaged storage tanks leaked an estimated 12,000 to 15,000 tonnes (more than 4&#160;million gallons) of oil into the eastern Mediterranean.<sup id="cite_ref-seattlepi_232-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattlepi-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> A 10&#160;km (6&#160;mi) wide oil slick covered 170&#160;km (105&#160;statute miles) of coastline,<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> and threatened <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>. The slick killed fish including the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_bluefin_tuna" title="Atlantic bluefin tuna">Atlantic bluefin tuna</a>, a species already nearing extinction in the Mediterranean, and threatened the habitat of the endangered green sea turtle.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> It also potentially increased the risk of cancer in humans. An additional 25,000 tons of oil burned at the power station, creating a "toxic cloud" that rained oil downwind.<sup id="cite_ref-seattlepi_232-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattlepi-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> The Lebanese government estimated it would take 10 years to recover from the damage of the strike. The UN estimated the cost for the initial clean-up at $64&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC:_Middle_East_crisis:_Facts_and_Figures_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_Middle_East_crisis:_Facts_and_Figures-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hezbollah rocket attacks caused numerous forest fires inside northern Israel, particularly on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Naftali_mountain_range&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Naftali mountain range (page does not exist)">Naftali mountain range</a> near <a href="/wiki/Kiryat_Shmona" title="Kiryat Shmona">Kiryat Shmona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Forestfire_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forestfire-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> As many as <span style="white-space:nowrap">16,500&#160;acres&#160;(67&#160;km²)</span> of land, including forests and grazing fields, were destroyed by Hezbollah rockets.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jewish_National_Fund" title="Jewish National Fund">Jewish National Fund</a> estimated that it would take 50 to 60 years to rehabilitate the forests.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Israeli bombing also caused significant damage to the <a href="/wiki/World_heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="World heritage site">world heritage sites</a> of Tyre and Byblos. In <a href="/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon" title="Tyre, Lebanon">Tyre</a> a Roman tomb was damaged and a fresco near the centre of the site collapsed. In <a href="/wiki/Byblos" title="Byblos">Byblos</a>, a medieval tower was damaged and Venetian period remains near the harbour were dramatically stained by the oil slick and were considered to be difficult to clean. Damage was also caused to remains at <a href="/wiki/Bint_Jbeil" title="Bint Jbeil">Bint Jbeil</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chamaa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chamaa (page does not exist)">Chamaa</a>, and to the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Bacchus" title="Temple of Bacchus">Temple of Bacchus</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baalbek" title="Baalbek">Baalbek</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_damage">Industrial damage</span></h3>
<table class="box-POV plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-POV" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" decoding="async" width="45" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="354" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">The <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutrality</a> of this section is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV_dispute" title="Wikipedia:NPOV dispute">disputed</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:2006_Lebanon_War##" title="Talk:2006 Lebanon War">talk page</a>. Please do not remove this message until <a href="/wiki/Template:POV#When_to_remove" title="Template:POV">conditions to do so are met</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Damage to various industries occurred during the war. This includes the country's largest dairy farm <a href="/wiki/Liban_Lait" title="Liban Lait">Liban Lait</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bekka" title="Bekka">Bekka</a> area, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maliban_Glassworks&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maliban Glassworks (page does not exist)">Maliban Glassworks</a> in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tannayel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tannayel (page does not exist)">Tannayel</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalal_Industries&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dalal Industries (page does not exist)">Dalal Industries</a> (a factory which produces prefabricated homes),<sup id="cite_ref-BekaaWorkingClass_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BekaaWorkingClass-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> a dealership for <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> two electricity transformers in <a href="/wiki/South_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="South Lebanon">south Lebanon</a> cutting off power to the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Tyre" class="mw-redirect" title="City of Tyre">city of Tyre</a><sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> and fuel tanks of an <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuel power plant">oil-fired power station</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jieh" title="Jieh">Jiyeh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> A report from the Lebanese Council for Development and Reconstruction (CDR) said that the IDF bombing campaign had destroyed more than 900 <a href="/wiki/Small_and_medium_enterprise" class="mw-redirect" title="Small and medium enterprise">small and medium enterprises</a> with damage to Lebanon's civilian infrastructure estimated close to $2.5 billion US. The material damage to the private sector was estimated at $200 million with an anticipated increase in that figure due to cancelled contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other repair and rebuilding costs resulting from the bombing include power supplies ($208m), telecoms ($99m), water ($74m) and military installations ($16m). The Lebanese national airline, <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Airlines" title="Middle East Airlines">MEA</a>, had also been grounded for the duration of the conflict. Agricultural activity, particularly in south Lebanon, was abandoned due to the fighting and bombing of the irrigation system.<sup id="cite_ref-ReconstructionCostsGuardian_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReconstructionCostsGuardian-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> Tourism, which accounts for 15% of Lebanon's <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a>, has been severely disrupted by the conflict. Damage to communal and business infrastructure, the Israeli-imposed sea and air <a href="/wiki/Blockade" title="Blockade">blockade</a> and continued instability is preventing and deterring tourists. Foreign visitors had been expected to bring in $2.5 to $3 billion US during 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-ReconstructionCostsGuardian_249-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReconstructionCostsGuardian-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>IDF bombing has damaged irrigation canals, open water channels, and underground water diversion pipes which run <a href="/wiki/Litani_River" title="Litani River">Litani River</a> water to more than 10,000 acres (40&#160;km²) of farmland, villages in southern Lebanon and the <a href="/wiki/Bekaa_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Bekaa Valley">Bekaa Valley</a>. These attacks have been criticised as an attempt to "lay claim to Lebanon's prime <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">watersheds</a>". Attacks on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Litani_Dam&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Litani Dam (page does not exist)">Litani Dam</a> were also criticised. Israeli officials explained the damage to the water infrastructures was unintentional and collateral to attacks on roads and bridges used by Hezbollah.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The international journalists' representative body, <a href="/wiki/Reporters_without_Borders" class="mw-redirect" title="Reporters without Borders">Reporters without Borders</a>, reported that, to its knowledge, the IDF had damaged transmitting equipment in the Satka area of Beirut and reduced the premises of <a href="/wiki/Al_Manar" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Manar">Al Manar</a> to ruins.<sup id="cite_ref-GlantzOW_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlantzOW-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> The IDF contend that the Al-Manar TV facilities which they bombed represent the <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a> arm of Hezbollah and were a legitimate target for the IDF military. Reporters Without Borders disputes this saying that the station "cannot be viewed as [a] military" target.<sup id="cite_ref-RWB_Beirut_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RWB_Beirut-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> A statement issued by the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Foreign_Ministry" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli Foreign Ministry">Israeli Foreign Ministry</a> read: "The Al-Manar station has for many years served as the main tool for propaganda and incitement by Hezbollah, and has also helped the organization recruit people into its ranks.”<sup id="cite_ref-GlantzOW_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlantzOW-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Committee_to_Protect_Journalists" title="Committee to Protect Journalists">Committee to Protect Journalists</a> responded by saying: "While Al-Manar may serve a propaganda function for Hezbollah, it does not appear based on a monitoring of its broadcasts today to be serving any discernible military function".<sup id="cite_ref-GlantzOW_251-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlantzOW-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_action_and_reaction">International action and reaction</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_involvement_in_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="Foreign involvement in the 2006 Lebanon War">Foreign involvement in the 2006 Lebanon War</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_reactions_to_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="International reactions to the 2006 Lebanon War">International reactions to the 2006 Lebanon War</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid_during_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="Humanitarian aid during the 2006 Lebanon War">Humanitarian aid during the 2006 Lebanon War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IsraelRallyLA2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/IsraelRallyLA2006.jpg/170px-IsraelRallyLA2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/IsraelRallyLA2006.jpg/255px-IsraelRallyLA2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/IsraelRallyLA2006.jpg/340px-IsraelRallyLA2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="453" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IsraelRallyLA2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Israel Solidarity Rally in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sydprot.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Sydprot.JPG/170px-Sydprot.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Sydprot.JPG/255px-Sydprot.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Sydprot.JPG/340px-Sydprot.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sydprot.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Lebanese protest in Sydney</div></div></div>
<p>The governments of the United States,<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> United Kingdom, Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> Australia, and Canada asserted Israel's right to <a href="/wiki/Self-defense" title="Self-defense">self-defense</a>. The United States government further responded by authorizing Israel's request for expedited shipment of <a href="/wiki/Precision-guided_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Precision-guided bomb">precision-guided bombs</a>, but did not announce the decision publicly.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> United States President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> said he thought the conflict was part of the "<a href="/wiki/War_on_Terrorism" class="mw-redirect" title="War on Terrorism">War on Terrorism</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> On 20 July 2006, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> voted overwhelmingly to support Israel's "right to defend itself".<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Among neighboring Middle Eastern nations, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, Syria, and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> voiced strong support for Hezbollah, while the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, Egypt, and <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> issued statements criticizing Hezbollah's actions<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> and declaring support for Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-HARTZAL_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HARTZAL-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> found Hezbollah entirely responsible.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, Jordan, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, Iraq, the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> agreed with the Saudi stance that Hezbollah's actions were "unexpected, inappropriate and irresponsible acts."<sup id="cite_ref-HARTZAL_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HARTZAL-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many worldwide <a href="/wiki/International_reactions_to_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="International reactions to the 2006 Lebanon War">protests</a> and demonstrations appealed for an immediate ceasefire on both sides and expressed concern for the heavy loss of civilian life on all sides. Other demonstrations were held exclusively in favor of Lebanon or Israel. Numerous newspaper advertising campaigns, <a href="/wiki/Short_message_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Short message service">SMS</a> and email appeals, and online petitions also occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Various foreign governments assisted the evacuation of their citizens from Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Allegations.2C_accusations_and_reports_of_war_crimes"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations,_accusations_and_reports_of_war_crimes">Allegations, accusations and reports of war crimes</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Allegations_of_war_crimes_in_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="Allegations of war crimes in the 2006 Lebanon War">Allegations of war crimes in the 2006 Lebanon War</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/International_incidents_during_the_2006_Lebanon_War" title="International incidents during the 2006 Lebanon War">International incidents during the 2006 Lebanon War</a></div>
<p>Under <a href="/wiki/International_humanitarian_law" title="International humanitarian law">international humanitarian law</a>, warring parties are obliged to <a href="/wiki/Distinction_(law)" title="Distinction (law)">distinguish between combatants and civilians</a>, ensure that attacks on legitimate military targets are <a href="/wiki/Proportionality_(law)" title="Proportionality (law)">proportional</a>, and guarantee that the military advantage of such attacks <a href="/wiki/Military_necessity" title="Military necessity">outweigh the possible harm done to civilians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hezb_cluster_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hezb_cluster-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> Violations of these laws are considered <a href="/wiki/War_crimes" class="mw-redirect" title="War crimes">war crimes</a>.
Various groups and individuals accused both Israel and Hezbollah of violations of these laws during the conflict, and warned of possible war crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_2006-07-20_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2006-07-20-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> These allegations included intentional attacks on <a href="/wiki/Civilian" title="Civilian">civilian populations</a> or infrastructure, <a href="/wiki/Proportionality_(international_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Proportionality (international law)">disproportionate</a> or indiscriminate attacks, the use of <a href="/wiki/Human_shield" title="Human shield">human shields</a>, and the use of prohibited weapons. No formal charges have been filed against either group.<sup id="cite_ref-AP_war_crimes_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP_war_crimes-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> called on both Hezbollah and Israel to end <a href="/wiki/Targeting_of_civilian_areas_in_the_2006_Lebanon_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Targeting of civilian areas in the 2006 Lebanon War">attacks on civilian areas</a> during the conflict,<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> and criticized attacks against civilian villages and infrastructure by Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-AI_evidence_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI_evidence-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> They also highlighted IDF use of <a href="/wiki/White_phosphorus_(weapon)" class="mw-redirect" title="White phosphorus (weapon)">white phosphorus shells</a> in Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-Rappaport_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rappaport-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> accused both parties of failing to distinguish between civilians and combatants, violating the <a href="/wiki/Distinction_(law)" title="Distinction (law)">principle of distinction</a>, and committing war crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-hezb_cluster_265-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hezb_cluster-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fatal_strikes_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fatal_strikes-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRW_war_crimes_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW_war_crimes-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Peter_Bouckaert&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Peter Bouckaert (page does not exist)">Peter Bouckaert</a>, a senior emergencies researcher for Human Rights Watch, stated that Hezbollah was "directly targeting civilians ... their aim is to kill Israeli civilians" and that Israel had not taken "the necessary precautions to distinguish between civilian and military targets."<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hezb_haifa_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hezb_haifa-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> They criticized Hezbollah's use of unguided <a href="/wiki/Katyusha_rocket_launcher" title="Katyusha rocket launcher">Katyusha</a> rockets, and Israel's use of unreliable <a href="/wiki/Cluster_bombs" class="mw-redirect" title="Cluster bombs">cluster bombs</a>&#160;– both too close to civilians areas&#160;– suggesting that they may have deliberately targeted civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-hezb_cluster_265-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hezb_cluster-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRW_CCW_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW_CCW-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> UN humanitarian chief <a href="/wiki/Jan_Egeland" title="Jan Egeland">Jan Egeland</a> said Israel's response violated international humanitarian law, and criticized Hezbollah for "cowardly blending... among women and children."<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> He also called Israel's use of over 100,000 cluster bombs "immoral". According to Egeland, 90% of such bombs were launched by Israel in the last 3 days of combat, when it was known that a UN resolution was on its way.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_IAF_Bombs_Katyusha_Rocket_Launchers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_IAF_Bombs_Katyusha_Rocket_Launchers.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_IAF_Bombs_Katyusha_Rocket_Launchers.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_IAF_Bombs_Katyusha_Rocket_Launchers.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_IAF_Bombs_Katyusha_Rocket_Launchers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_IAF_Bombs_Katyusha_Rocket_Launchers.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_IAF_Bombs_Katyusha_Rocket_Launchers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2357" data-file-height="1763" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_IAF_Bombs_Katyusha_Rocket_Launchers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>IAF targeting a Katyusha rocket launcher</div></div></div>
<p>Israel said that it tried to avoid civilians, and had distributed leaflets calling on civilian residents to evacuate,<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> but that Hezbollah stored weapons in and fired from civilian areas, making those areas legitimate targets,<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> and used civilians as human shields.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> Amnesty International and Human Rights Watch found cases where Hezbollah did fire rockets from, and store weapons in, populated areas and deploy its forces among the civilian population; however, both say that is not conclusive evidence of the intent to use civilians as human shields.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_280-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRW2_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW2-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> HRW stated that "the IDF struck a large number of private homes of civilian Hezbollah members during the war, as well as various civilian Hezbollah-run institutions such as schools, welfare agencies, banks, shops and political offices."<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Although Israel maintained that the civilian infrastructure was "hijacked" by Hezbollah and used for military purposes,<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> but Amnesty International identified the destruction of entire civilian neighbourhoods and villages by Israeli forces, attacks on bridges with no apparent strategic value, and attacks on infrastructure indispensable to the survival of the civilian population,<sup id="cite_ref-AI_evidence_269-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI_evidence-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> and questioned whether the "military advantage anticipated from destroying" civilian infrastructure had been "measured against the likely effect on civilians."<sup id="cite_ref-AI_dmg_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI_dmg-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> They also stated that the Israeli actions suggested a "policy of punishing both the Lebanese government and the civilian population."<sup id="cite_ref-AI_dmg_290-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI_dmg-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Al-Jazeera" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Jazeera">Al-Jazeera</a> reported at the time: "Foreign journalists based in Lebanon also reported that the <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a> militia chose to fight from civilian areas and had on occasion prevented Lebanese civilians from fleeing conflict-hit areas of south Lebanon. <a href="/wiki/Al-Manar" title="Al-Manar">Al-Manar</a>, Hezbollah's satellite channel, also showed footage of Hezbollah firing rockets from civilian areas and produced animated graphics showing how Hezbollah fired rockets at Israeli cities from inside villages in southern Lebanon."
</p><p>Images obtained by the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Herald_Sun" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday Herald Sun">Sunday Herald Sun</a></i> show that "Hezbollah is waging war amid suburbia. The images ... show Hezbollah using high-density residential areas as launch pads for rockets and heavy-calibre weapons. Dressed in civilian clothing so they can quickly disappear, the militants carrying automatic assault rifles and ride in on trucks mounted with cannon."<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Amnesty International stated, however, that the volume of civilian casualties and damage to civilian infrastructure suggested that Israel was not just trying to target Hezbollah fighters. An AI spokesperson, Kate Gilmore, said that "[t]he pattern, scope and scale of the attacks makes Israel's claim that this was 'collateral damage', simply not credible".<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> "The evidence strongly suggests that the extensive destruction of power and water plants, as well as the transport infrastructure vital for food and other humanitarian relief, was deliberate and an integral part of a military strategy," Gilmore said.
</p><p>On 24 July 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/Haaretz" title="Haaretz">Haaretz</a></i> reported that the official Israeli inquiry into the war "is to include the examination of claims that the IDF committed war crimes during last summer's fighting."<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 6 September 2007 Human Rights Watch report found that most of the civilian deaths in Lebanon resulted from "indiscriminate Israeli airstrikes", and found that Israeli aircraft targeted vehicles carrying fleeing civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> In a statement issued before the report's release, the human rights organization said there was no basis to the Israeli government's claim that civilian casualties resulted from Hezbollah guerrillas using civilians as shields. <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Roth" title="Kenneth Roth">Kenneth Roth</a>, Human Rights Watch executive director, said there were only "rare" cases of Hezbollah operating in civilian villages. "To the contrary, once the war started, most Hizbollah(sic) military officials and even many political officials left the villages," he said. "Most Hizbollah(sic) military activity was conducted from prepared positions outside Lebanese villages in the hills and valleys around." Roth also noted that "Hezbollah fighters often didn't carry their weapons in the open or regularly wear military uniforms, which made them a hard target to identify. But this doesn't justify the IDF's failure to distinguish between civilians and combatants, and if in doubt to treat a person as a civilian, as the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws of war">laws of war</a> require."<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On its final report, issued on 30 January 2008, the Israeli government's <a href="/wiki/Winograd_Commission" title="Winograd Commission">Winograd Commission</a> concluded that the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> did not commit violations or war crimes, as alleged by the <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, and other NGOs. The Commission claimed that the evidence shows that the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> did not target civilians, in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> and to denunciations by NGOs, and explained that terms like "war crimes" are without basis.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> This report also acknowledged that Israel used cluster bombs illegally, stating that "Israel must consider whether it wants to continue using cluster bombs in the future, because its current manner of employing them does not conform to international law."<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War_photographs_controversies" title="2006 Lebanon War photographs controversies">2006 Lebanon War photographs controversies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adnan_Hajj_photographs_controversy" title="Adnan Hajj photographs controversy">Adnan Hajj photographs controversy</a></div>
<p>The 2007 report "'War to the Last Moment': The Israeli Media in the Second Lebanon War" by the Israeli media monitoring NGO <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.keshev.org.il/">Keshev</a> (trans. "Awareness")<sup id="cite_ref-Keshev1_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keshev1-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> stated that the Israeli media "except for a few exceptional instances ... covered the war in an almost entirely mobilized manner" serving more to support the goals of the Israeli government and IDF than to objectively report the news. "The media created a general atmosphere of complete and absolute support and justification of the war, and systematically suppressed questions that arose as early as the first day of fighting. ... The criticism gradually increased toward the end of the war-as it became clearer that the IDF was not managing to win. But the general spirit of the war coverage, in the broad strategic sense, as utterly uncritical." Keshev's report documents a post-war memo from the Deputy CEO of Marketing for the Hebrew newspaper <a href="/wiki/Maariv" title="Maariv">Maariv</a> to Maariv employees which states, in part, that 
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Even when we had problematic material related to the management of the war ... we restrained ourselves. In a certain sense, we betrayed our role as journalists, but we did so because we took national, patriotic considerations into account and decided that in the event of war, and certainly a war which was not progressing as it should and was going awry, we were part of the Country; that it was permissible, and even required of us, to postpone disputes and criticism; and that we did not have to apologize, or to feel abashed, for our support and backing of the Army and the Government.<sup id="cite_ref-Keshev1_298-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keshev1-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>According to the report, "significant coverage of the decision-making process was almost entirely absent in Israel's media" at the beginning of the war and reports on the status of Israelis living in the North who did not receive proper governmental support were marginalized. Further, the report states that the media unreasonably centered on the question of the loyalties of Arab-Israelis in the North instead of focusing on inadequate provision of services by the state. The report acknowledges that the Israeli media reported on Lebanese suffering, But states that it divorced the suffering from the IDF operations causing it. Finally, with regard to diplomacy, Israeli media buried the stories on negotiations to reflect the derision held by decision-makers toward a diplomatic solution.<sup id="cite_ref-Keshev1_298-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keshev1-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 July 2006 Hezbollah Press Officer Hussein Nabulsi took CNN's <a href="/wiki/Nic_Robertson" title="Nic Robertson">Nic Robertson</a> on an exclusive tour of southern Beirut. Robertson noted that despite his minder's anxiety about explosions in the area, it was clear that Hezbollah had sophisticated media relations and were in control of the situation. Hezbollah designated the places that they went to, and the journalists "certainly didn't have time to go into the houses or lift up the rubble to see what was underneath." According to his reports, there was no doubt that the bombs were hitting Hezbollah facilities, and while there appeared to be "a lot of civilian damage, a lot of civilian properties," he reiterated that he could not verify the civilian nature of the destroyed buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-reliable_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reliable-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several media commentators and journalists have alleged an intentionally distorted coverage of the events, in favour of Hezbollah, by means of <a href="/wiki/Photo_manipulation" title="Photo manipulation">photo manipulation</a>, staging by Hezbollah or by journalists, and false or misleading captioning.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>'s Charlie Moore described a Hezbollah press tour of a bombed-out area in southern Beirut on 23 July 2006 as a "dog-and-pony show" due to perceived staging, misrepresentation of the nature of the destroyed areas, and strict directives about when and with whom interviews could take place.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> In the same interview CNN's <a href="/wiki/John_Roberts_(television_reporter)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Roberts (television reporter)">John Roberts</a>, reporting from an Israeli artillery battery on the Lebanese border, stated that he had to take everything he was told&#160;– either by the IDF or Hezbollah&#160;– "with a grain of salt," citing mutual recriminations of civilian targeting which he was unable to verify independently.<sup id="cite_ref-reliable_299-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reliable-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> As another example, <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> withdrew over 900 photographs by <a href="/wiki/Adnan_Hajj_photographs_controversy" title="Adnan Hajj photographs controversy">Adnan Hajj</a>, a Lebanese freelance photographer, after he admitted to digitally adding and darkening smoke spirals in photographs of an attack on Beirut.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> Photographs submitted to Reuters and <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> showed one Lebanese woman mourning on two different pictures taken by two photographers, allegedly taken two weeks apart.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> It is "common practice to send more than one photographer to an incident".<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Social and online media were important for providing alternate means of creating and disseminating accounts and political commentary. For example, Lebanese blogger Fink Ployd maintained the blog <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://bloggingbeirut.com/">BloggingBeirut.com</a>, posting images, audio files, and testimony from Lebanon, particularly from Lebanese Arab youth.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Swedish politician <a href="/wiki/Lars_Adaktusson" title="Lars Adaktusson">Lars Adaktusson</a>, who worked as a journalist in Israel for national news outlet <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Television" title="Sveriges Television">Sveriges Television (SVT)</a> at the time of the war, stated in a 2017 presentation that he was ordered by SVT management to report that armed hostilities had been started by Israel irrespective of the facts. Also he was ordered not to report Hizbollah rocket attacks on Israeli civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-inblick2feb2017_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inblick2feb2017-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reviews_of_the_conflict">Reviews of the conflict</span></h2>
<p>Following the UN-brokered ceasefire, there were mixed responses on who had gained or lost the most in the war. Iran and Syria proclaimed a victory for Hezbollah<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> while Olmert declared that the war was a success for Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-claim_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-claim-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lebanon">Lebanon</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hezbollah_territory.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Hezbollah_territory.JPG/220px-Hezbollah_territory.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Hezbollah_territory.JPG/330px-Hezbollah_territory.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Hezbollah_territory.JPG/440px-Hezbollah_territory.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1840" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hezbollah_territory.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A sign erected after the 2006 Lebanon war in <a href="/wiki/South_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="South Lebanon">South Lebanon</a> which displays rockets and Hezbollah leader <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Nasrallah" title="Hassan Nasrallah">Hassan Nasrallah</a></div></div></div>
<p>At the outbreak of hostilities, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Fouad_Siniora" title="Fouad Siniora">Fouad Siniora</a> promised to rein in Hezbollah in an effort to stop Israel's offensive. Saniora said that there could be no sovereign state of Lebanon without the group's disarming. The former President of Lebanon <a href="/wiki/Amin_Gemayel" class="mw-redirect" title="Amin Gemayel">Amin Gemayel</a>, a longtime critic of Hezbollah said, "Hezbollah took a unilateral action, but its repercussions will affect the entire country."<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews.com_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews.com-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup>
The war deepened the longtime divide in Lebanon over Hezbollah's role. Many admired the organization for being the sole group to fight against Israel. Others considered it to be a dangerous militia that executes Iran and Syria policies in Lebanon. The divide over Hezbollah followed mostly sectarian lines, with <a href="/wiki/Shias" class="mw-redirect" title="Shias">Shias</a> largely supporting the group and <a href="/wiki/Sunnis" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunnis">Sunnis</a>, Christians and <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druse</a> mostly opposing it.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews.com_309-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews.com-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 August 2006, Nasrallah said in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Al_Jadeed" title="Al Jadeed">New TV</a> that the abduction of the two soldiers did not cause the war. It only advanced a long planned war for a few months. But he added: "If there was even a 1 percent chance that the July 11 capturing operation would have led to a war like the one that happened, would you have done it? I would say no, absolutely not, for humanitarian, moral, social, security, military, and political reasons. […] What happened is not an issue of a reaction to a capturing operation… what happened was already planned for. The fact that it happened in July has averted a situation that would have been a lot worse, had the war been launched in October."<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 September 2006, some eight hundred thousand Hezbollah supporters gathered in Beirut for a rally at which Nasrallah stated that Hezbollah had achieved a "divine and strategic victory."<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_800_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_800-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span></h3>
<p>Within hours of Israeli's bombing of Lebanon on 13 July 2006, hundreds of protesters gathered in <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> to oppose the war.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> On 22 July, about 2,000 people, including many Palestinian Arab citizens of Israel, demanded an end to the offensive during a protest march in Tel Aviv's <a href="/wiki/Rabin_Square" title="Rabin Square">Rabin Square</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> On 5 August, some Israelis demonstrated in Tel Aviv, including former <a href="/wiki/Knesset" title="Knesset">Knesset</a> members of the <a href="/wiki/Meretz" title="Meretz">Meretz</a> party, <a href="/wiki/Mossi_Raz" title="Mossi Raz">Mossi Raz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naomi_Hazan" class="mw-redirect" title="Naomi Hazan">Naomi Hazan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yael_Dayan" title="Yael Dayan">Yael Dayan</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Initially, in a poll by an Israeli radio station, <a href="/wiki/Israelis" title="Israelis">Israelis</a> were split on the outcome with the majority believing that no one won.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> By 25 August 63% of Israelis polled wanted Olmert to resign due to his handling of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerusalem Post">Jerusalem Post</a></i> said that " if you fail to win, you lose" and that as "Hezbollah survived, it won the war."<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Olmert admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Knesset" title="Knesset">Knesset</a> that there were mistakes in the war in Lebanon,<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> though he framed UN Security Council resolution 1701 as an accomplishment for Israel that would bring home the captured soldiers, and said that the operations had altered the regional strategic balance vis-à-vis Hezbollah.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_General_Staff_(Israel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief of General Staff (Israel)">Israeli Chief of Staff</a> <a href="/wiki/Dan_Halutz" title="Dan Halutz">Dan Halutz</a> admitted to failings in the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> On 15 August, Israeli government and defense officials called for Halutz's resignation following a <a href="/wiki/Dan_Halutz#Investment_portfolio_scandal" title="Dan Halutz">stock scandal</a> in which he admitted selling stocks hours before the start of the Israeli offensive.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> Halutz subsequently resigned on 17 January 2007.
</p><p>On 21 August, a group of demobilized Israel reserve soldiers and parents of soldiers killed in the fighting started <a href="/wiki/2006_Israeli_reserve_soldiers%27_protest" title="2006 Israeli reserve soldiers&#39; protest">a movement</a> calling for the resignation of Olmert and the establishment of a state commission of <a href="/wiki/Public_inquiry" title="Public inquiry">inquiry</a>. They set up a <a href="/wiki/Protest_tent" class="mw-redirect" title="Protest tent">protest tent</a> opposite the Knesset and grew to over 2,000 supporters by 25 August,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> including the influential <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Quality_Government_in_Israel" title="Movement for Quality Government in Israel">Movement for Quality Government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> On 28 August, Olmert <a href="/wiki/2006_Israeli_reserve_soldiers%27_protest#Prospects_for_a_state_commission" title="2006 Israeli reserve soldiers&#39; protest">announced</a> that there would be no independent state or governmental commission of inquiry, but two internal inspection probes, one to investigate the political echelon and one to examine the IDF, and likely a third commission to examine the <a href="/wiki/Home_Front" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Front">Home Front</a>, to be announced at a later date. These would have a more limited mandate and less authority than a single inquiry commission headed by a retired judge.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> The political and military committees were to be headed by former director of <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">Mossad</a> <a href="/wiki/Nahum_Admoni" title="Nahum Admoni">Nahum Admoni</a> and former Chief of Staff <a href="/wiki/Amnon_Lipkin-Shahak" title="Amnon Lipkin-Shahak">Amnon Lipkin-Shahak</a>, respectively.
