Critics argued that these committees amount to a <a href="/wiki/Whitewash" title="Whitewash">whitewash</a>, due to their limited authority, limited investigatory scope, their self-appointed basis, and that neither would be headed by a retired judge.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Due to these pressures, on 11 October, Admoni was replaced by retired justice <a href="/wiki/Eliyahu_Winograd" title="Eliyahu Winograd">Eliyahu Winograd</a> as chair of the political probe, and the probe itself was elevated to the status of governmental commission with near-state commission mandate: the <a href="/wiki/Winograd_Commission" title="Winograd Commission">Winograd Commission</a>. On 12 September, former defense minister <a href="/wiki/Moshe_Arens" title="Moshe Arens">Moshe Arens</a> spoke of "the defeat of Israel" in calling for a state committee of inquiry. He said that Israel had lost "to a very small group of people, 5,000 Hezbollah fighters, which should have been no match at all for the IDF", and stated that the conflict could have "some very fateful consequences for the future."<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> Disclosing his intent to shortly resign, <a href="/wiki/Ilan_Harari" title="Ilan Harari">Ilan Harari</a>, the IDF's chief education officer, stated at a conference of senior IDF officers that Israel lost the war, becoming the first senior active duty officer to publicly state such an opinion.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> IDF Major General <a href="/wiki/Yiftah_Ron-Tal" title="Yiftah Ron-Tal">Yiftah Ron Tal</a>, on 4 October 2006 became the second and highest ranking serving officer to express his opinion that the IDF failed "to win the day in the battle against Hezbollah" as well as calling for Lt. Gen. Dan Halutz' resignation.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup> Ron-Tal was subsequently fired for making those and other critical comments.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, Eyal Zisser, director of the <a href="/wiki/Moshe_Dayan_Center_for_Middle_Eastern_and_African_Studies" title="Moshe Dayan Center for Middle Eastern and African Studies">Moshe Dayan Center for Middle Eastern and African Studies</a> at Tel Aviv University, took a contrary position and expressed the view that the war was in fact a strategic success for Israel and a Hezbollah defeat. He noted that Hezbollah had "lost about a third of its elite fighting force" and that "despite mistakes made by the IDF in conducting the military campaign, Israeli soldiers triumphed in every face-to-face battle with Hezbollah." He concluded that "as time passes, the severity of the blow suffered by Lebanon and its people from the 2006 war becomes clear."<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2007, the Committee decided to name the war the "Second Lebanon War", a decision that was subsequently approved by the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Israel" title="Cabinet of Israel">Israeli cabinet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Barak" title="Ehud Barak">Ehud Barak</a>, the replacement defense minister for Peretz, stated that the conflict failed to disarm Hezbollah, and that the group is increasingly entrenched in South Lebanon, further stating that "Hezbollah is stronger than ever and has more rockets than at the outbreak of the Lebanon war in the summer of 2006"<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> but he later noted that "[Israeli] deterrence still exists."<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> The IDF's Northern Command cited this deterrence as one reason Hezbollah did not fire any rockets into Israel during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Cast_Lead" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Cast Lead">Operation Cast Lead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Israeli military historian <a href="/wiki/Martin_van_Creveld" title="Martin van Creveld">Martin van Creveld</a> stated that Israel's war against Hezbollah was indeed "marked by a long series of failures" but he criticized the <a href="/wiki/Winograd_Commission" title="Winograd Commission">Winograd Commission</a> for its failure to take into account the substantial achievements of the war. He noted that hundreds of Hezbollah fighters were killed in the war, and that the organization had "the fight knocked out of it", since following the war, Israel experienced a level of calm on its Lebanon border not seen since the mid-1960s. He also noted that Hezbollah was "thrown out of South Lebanon", and was replaced by "a fairly robust United Nations peacekeeping force" to prevent its return.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>IDF Maj.-Gen. (res.) <a href="/wiki/Yaakov_Amidror" title="Yaakov Amidror">Yaakov Amidror</a> highlighted the number of Hezbollah militants killed, the quick military response to Hezbollah's long-range rocket attacks, the post-war replacement of Hezbollah by the Lebanese Army and UNIFIL in southern Lebanon, and Iran's loss of Hezbollah as a deterrent against an Israeli first strike following the war.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Friedman" title="Thomas Friedman">Thomas Friedman</a> concurred, stating that the war was a "huge strategic loss for Hezbollah", and contrasted the billions in damage suffered by Hezbollah and Lebanon with the "relatively minor damage" suffered by Israel, which enjoyed an economic "growth spurt" immediately following the war.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Winograd_Commission_report">Winograd Commission report</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Winograd_Commission" title="Winograd Commission">Winograd Commission</a></div>
<p>According to the Winograd Commission report, the Second Lebanon War was regarded as a "missed opportunity" and that "Israel initiated a long war, which ended without a defined military victory". The report continued to state that "a semi-military organization of a few thousand men resisted, for a few weeks, the strongest army in the Middle East, which enjoyed full <a href="/wiki/Air_superiority" class="mw-redirect" title="Air superiority">air superiority</a> and size and technology advantages." Furthermore, <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>'s rocket attacks continued throughout the war and the IDF did not provide an effective response to it. Following a long period of using standoff firepower and limited ground activities, the IDF launched a large-scale ground offensive close to the UN Security Council's resolution which imposed a cease-fire. "This offensive did not result in military gains and was not completed."
</p><p>Later in the Report, the Commission stated that "[a] decision [was] made in the night of 12 July to react (to the capturing) with immediate and substantive military action and to set ... ambitious goals." This decision had immediate repercussions in that subsequent decisions were limited mainly to a choice between a) "a short, painful and unexpected blow on Hezbollah" and b) "to bring about a significant change of the reality in the South of Lebanon with a large ground operation,[occupying] ... the South of Lebanon and 'cleaning' it of Hezbollah." "The fact Israel went to war before it decided which option to select and without an exit strategy, all these constituted serious failures of the decision making process." As for achievements, the Commission reported that "SC resolution 1701, and the fact that it was adopted unanimously, were an achievement for Israel."<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bush_delivers_Middle_East_crisis_statement_w_Rice_Aug_7_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Bush_delivers_Middle_East_crisis_statement_w_Rice_Aug_7_2006.jpg/220px-Bush_delivers_Middle_East_crisis_statement_w_Rice_Aug_7_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Bush_delivers_Middle_East_crisis_statement_w_Rice_Aug_7_2006.jpg/330px-Bush_delivers_Middle_East_crisis_statement_w_Rice_Aug_7_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Bush_delivers_Middle_East_crisis_statement_w_Rice_Aug_7_2006.jpg/440px-Bush_delivers_Middle_East_crisis_statement_w_Rice_Aug_7_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="514" data-file-height="364" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bush_delivers_Middle_East_crisis_statement_w_Rice_Aug_7_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> declared that Hezbollah lost the war and that "There's going to be a new power in the south of Lebanon".<sup id="cite_ref-denverpost1_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-denverpost1-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In the aftermath of the conflict US President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George Bush</a> said that Hezbollah was responsible for starting the war, and that the group suffered a defeat at the hands of Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-bushspeech_337-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bushspeech-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> He dismissed claims of victory by Hezbollah leaders, asking: "how can you claim victory when at one time you were a state within a state, safe within southern Lebanon, and now you're going to be replaced by a Lebanese Army and an international force?"<sup id="cite_ref-bushspeech_337-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bushspeech-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> In his 2010 memoir, <i><a href="/wiki/Decision_Points" title="Decision Points">Decision Points</a></i>, Bush wrote that Israel had weakened Hezbollah and secured its northern border, but that Israel's "shaky military performance" cost it international credibility. He also said that Israel "mishandled its opportunity", and that some of the sites it attacked were of "questionable military value".<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a speech given on 15 August 2006, Syrian President <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a> claimed that the Arab resistance against Israel would continue to grow stronger, saying, "Your weapons, warplanes, rockets and even <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_Israel" title="Nuclear weapons and Israel">your atomic bomb</a> will not protect you in the future."<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> magazine concluded that by surviving this asymmetrical military conflict with Israel, Hezbollah effectively emerged with a military and political victory from this conflict. They cite the facts that Hezbollah was able to sustain defenses on Lebanese soil and inflict unmitigated rocket attacks on Israeli civilians in the face of a punishing air and land campaign by the IDF.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Matt M. Matthews, a military historian at the Combat Studies Institute of the U.S. Army <a href="/wiki/Command_and_General_Staff_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Command and General Staff College">Command and General Staff College</a> praised Hezbollah <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">paramilitaries</a> and reflected on what he described as "the lackluster performance of the IDF." He attributed this to several factors including (Lieutenant-General and Chief of the IDF General Staff) Halutz's steadfast confidence in air power coupled with continuing <a href="/wiki/Counterinsurgency" class="mw-redirect" title="Counterinsurgency">COIN</a> operations against the Palestinians at the expense of training for major combat operations.<sup id="cite_ref-csi_341-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csi-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The US <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Research_Service" title="Congressional Research Service">Congressional Research Service</a> found that although Hezbollah's military capabilities may have been substantially reduced, its long-term potential as a guerrilla movement appeared to remain intact: "Observers note that Hezbollah's leaders have been able to claim a level of 'victory' simply by virtue of not having decisively 'lost'."<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Military analyst and former IDF general Giora Eiland concluded that, though outgunned and outnumbered, Hezbollah managed to hold off Israel's advanced armed forces and proved its ability to damage Israel by launching rockets at its territory until the end of the war. He estimates that Hezbollah's destructive capabilities have increased in the years after the war and that the group is capable to inflict "far worse damage on the Israeli homefront" than in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> An Israeli official warned that combat with Hezbollah will be very bloody and Lebanon would sustain heavy damage in any future war.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2007 <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> documentary, <i>Hunting for Hezbollah</i>, BBC <i><a href="/wiki/This_World_(television_programme)" class="mw-redirect" title="This World (television programme)">This World</a></i> reporter Emeka Onono referred to Israel's inability to eliminate Hezbollah as a "humiliation for Israel's supposedly all-powerful army," and he went on to claim that Hezbollah's survival propelled it to hero status throughout many Muslim nations.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>British military historian <a href="/wiki/John_Keegan" title="John Keegan">John Keegan</a> stated that the outcome of the war was "misreported as an Israeli defeat" due to anti-Israel bias in the international media. He concluded that Hezbollah had suffered heavy losses, and that a cease-fire came into effect before Israel could completely dislodge Hezbollah from its positions. He also stated that the casualties sustained by Israel during the war had alarmed the Israeli Government and High Command because Israel's small population is acutely vulnerable to losses in battle.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Charles_Krauthammer" title="Charles Krauthammer">Charles Krauthammer</a>, a syndicated columnist and political commentator, citing an interview by which Nasrallah admitted that he would not have captured the soldiers had he known that it would lead to war, wrote, "Nasrallah's admission, vastly underplayed in the West, makes clear what Lebanese already knew. Hezbollah may have won the propaganda war, but on the ground it lost. Badly." He noted that Hezbollah's entrenched infrastructure along Israel's border was shattered and would not be easily rebuilt due to the presence of the Lebanese Army and a robust UNIFIL force, hundreds of Hezbollah's best fighters were killed in the war, and that many Lebanese were angry with Hezbollah for provoking a war which largely devastated the country.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> stated that the war had been "widely seen as a disaster for the Israeli military". It further reported that the US Defense Department had sent as many as a dozen teams to interview Israeli officers who had fought in the war, to learn the lessons of the Israeli army's failures during the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Michael Young, opinion page editor at the Lebanese <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Star_(Lebanon)" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily Star (Lebanon)">Daily Star</a></i> newspaper, stated that Hezbollah turned "the stench of defeat into the smell of victory", through clever use of its propaganda machine. He suggested that Hezbollah had "hoodwinked" pundits who believed that Hezbollah was victorious, and opined that "one dreads to imagine what Hezbollah would recognize as a military loss."<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>American military strategist and historian <a href="/wiki/Edward_Luttwak" title="Edward Luttwak">Edward Luttwak</a> drew comparisons with the 1973 Yom Kippur War, where what initially looked like an Israeli setback later turned out to be an IDF victory and an Arab defeat. He stated that although some IDF tanks were penetrated by missiles, they also largely limited IDF casualties, and that Hezbollah had failed to inflict massive losses on the IDF and to kill large numbers of Israelis in rocket attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge University">Cambridge</a> professor and Peterhouse Fellow <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Simms" title="Brendan Simms">Brendan Simms</a> summed up the war this way; "Hezbollah have suffered a setback (but are too clever to admit it) and the Israelis have scored a long-term success (but are too narrow-minded to realize it)."<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Journalist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Totten" title="Michael Totten">Michael Totten</a> wrote that "Hezbollah lost and Hezbollah knows it." He questioned why Hezbollah did not attack Israel when the IDF attacked Hamas in <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza</a> in 2008, and noted that most of Nasrallah's supporters "want Hezbollah to deter Israeli invasions, not to invite Israeli invasions". Totten concluded that Nasrallah's boasts "play well in much of the Arab world", but that the 2006 "victory" seemed "empty at home."<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Armin Rosen, Defense and military advisor wrote at Business Insider that the 2006 Lebanon War was "widely remembered as one of the worst debacles in the history of the Israeli military", but remarked that it established Israeli deterrence against Hezbollah.<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_and_political_repercussions">Financial and political repercussions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/2008_conflict_in_Lebanon" title="2008 conflict in Lebanon">2008 conflict in Lebanon</a></div>
<p>The fighting resulted in a huge financial setback for Lebanon, with an official estimate of a fall in growth from +6% to 2% and US$5&#160;Billion (22% of GDP)<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup> in direct and indirect costs, while the cost for Israel was estimated at US$3.5&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> Indirect costs to Israel include a cut in growth by 0.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> and the cost to tourism was estimated at 0.4% of Israel's GDP in the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> According to Imad Salamey in <i>The Government and Politics of Lebanon</i>, the main casualty was the fragile unity between Lebanon's sectarian and political groups.<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-ceasefire_events">Post-ceasefire events</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Military_Operations_in_the_2006_Lebanon_War#Post-ceasefire_events" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Military Operations in the 2006 Lebanon War">Timeline of Military Operations in the 2006 Lebanon War §&#160;Post-ceasefire events</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Infographic,_Hezbollah%27s_Arsenal_of_Rockets.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Infographic%2C_Hezbollah%27s_Arsenal_of_Rockets.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Infographic%2C_Hezbollah%27s_Arsenal_of_Rockets.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="481" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Infographic%2C_Hezbollah%27s_Arsenal_of_Rockets.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Infographic%2C_Hezbollah%27s_Arsenal_of_Rockets.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Infographic%2C_Hezbollah%27s_Arsenal_of_Rockets.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Infographic%2C_Hezbollah%27s_Arsenal_of_Rockets.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="1094" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Infographic,_Hezbollah%27s_Arsenal_of_Rockets.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An infographic produced by the Israel Defence Force criticizing Hezbollah’s violations of United Nations Security Council Resolution 1701. The resolution calls for Hezbollah to remain disarmed and bans paramilitary activity south of the <a href="/wiki/Litani_River" title="Litani River">Litani River</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In the days following 14 August 2006 ceasefire, Hezbollah launched dozens of rockets and mortars inside southern Lebanon, which Israel did not respond to, though there were several instances where Israeli troops killed armed Hezbollah members approaching their positions.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup> Israeli warplanes continued conducting numerous flyovers and maneuvers above southern Lebanon, which Israel said did not violate the ceasefire.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup> On 19 August 2006, Israel <a href="/wiki/Operation_Sharp_and_Smooth" title="Operation Sharp and Smooth">launched a raid</a> in Lebanon's eastern <a href="/wiki/Beqaa_Valley" title="Beqaa Valley">Beqaa Valley</a> it says was aimed at disrupting Hezbollah's weapons supply from Syria and Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_Beka_raid_364-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Beka_raid-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup> Lebanese officials "said the Israelis were apparently seeking a guerrilla target in a school."<sup id="cite_ref-raidendangers_365-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raidendangers-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup> Israel's aerial and commando operations were criticised by Kofi Annan as violations of the ceasefire, which he said they had conducted the majority of, and he also protested the continued embargo. France, then leading UNIFIL, also issued criticism of the flyovers, which it interpreted as aggressive.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> Israel argued that "[t]he cease-fire is based on <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1701" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1701">(UN resolution) 1701</a> which calls for an international arms embargo against Hezbollah," and said the embargo could be lifted after full implementation of the cease-fire<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_Beka_raid_364-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Beka_raid-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup> but Annan said that UNIFIL would only interdict arms at Lebanon's request.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> On 7 September 2006 and 8 September 2006 respectively, aviation and naval blockades were lifted.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup> In the second half of September Hezbollah claimed victory and asserted an improvement in their position, and they redeployed to some positions on the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Line_(Lebanon)" title="Blue Line (Lebanon)">border</a><sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theguardian20k_375-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian20k-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> as Israel completed its withdrawal from Lebanon save border-straddling <a href="/wiki/Ghajar" title="Ghajar">Ghajar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn.com_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup> On 3 October, an Israeli fighter penetrated the 2-nautical-mile (4&#160;km) defence perimeter of the French frigate <i><a href="/wiki/Courbet_(F_712)" class="mw-redirect" title="Courbet (F 712)">Courbet</a></i> without answering radio calls, triggering a diplomatic incident.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 October, six <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force" title="Israeli Air Force">Israeli</a> <a href="/wiki/F-16" class="mw-redirect" title="F-16">F-16s</a> flew over a <a href="/wiki/German_Navy" title="German Navy">German Navy</a> vessel patrolling off Israel's coast just south of the Lebanese border. The German Defence Ministry said that the planes had given off infrared decoys and one of the aircraft had fired two shots into the air, which had not been specifically aimed. The Israeli military said that a German helicopter took off from the vessel without having coordinated this with Israel, and denied vehemently having fired any shots at the vessel and said "as of now" it also had no knowledge of the jets launching flares over it. Israeli Defence Minister <a href="/wiki/Amir_Peretz" title="Amir Peretz">Amir Peretz</a> telephoned his German counterpart <a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Jung" title="Franz Josef Jung">Franz Josef Jung</a> to clarify that 'Israel has no intention to carry out any aggressive actions' against the German peacekeeping forces in Lebanon, who are there as part of <a href="/wiki/UNIFIL" class="mw-redirect" title="UNIFIL">UNIFIL</a> to enforce an arms embargo against Hezbollah. Germany confirmed the consultations, and that both sides were interested in maintaining good cooperation.<sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 December 2006, UN Secretary-General Kofi Annan submitted a report to the Security Council president maintaining "there were no serious incidents or confrontations" since the cease-fire in August 2006. He did, however, note that peacekeepers reported air violations by Israel "almost on a daily basis," which Israel maintained were a security measure related to continuing Syrian and Iranian arms shipments to Hezbollah, and evidence of the presence of unauthorized armed personnel, assets, and weapons in Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-iht_vio_challenge_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iht_vio_challenge-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In one case, a UNIFIL demining team was challenged by two Hezbollah members in combat uniforms armed with <a href="/wiki/AK-47" title="AK-47">AK-47 rifles</a>; UNIFIL notified the Lebanese army, who arrested three suspects the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-iht_vio_challenge_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iht_vio_challenge-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> There were also "13 instances where UNIFIL came across unauthorized arms or related material in its area of operation", including the discovery of 17 katyusha rockets and several improvised explosive devices in <a href="/wiki/Rachaiya_El-Foukhar" class="mw-redirect" title="Rachaiya El-Foukhar">Rachaiya El-Foukhar</a>, and the discovery of a weapons cache containing seven missiles, three rocket launchers, and a substantial amount of ammunition in the area of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bourhoz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bourhoz (page does not exist)">Bourhoz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iht_vio_challenge_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iht_vio_challenge-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ynet_annan_report_384-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ynet_annan_report-384">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup> Annan also reported that as of 20 November 2006, 822 Israeli cluster bomb strike sites had been recorded,<sup id="cite_ref-ynet_annan_report_384-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ynet_annan_report-384">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup> with 60,000 cluster bomblets having been cleared by the <a href="/wiki/Mine_Action_Coordination_Center" title="Mine Action Coordination Center">UN Mine Action Coordination Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The months after the hostilities saw major upheaval in the Israeli military and political echelon, with the spate of high-ranking resignations including <a href="/wiki/Ramatkal" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramatkal">Chief of General Staff</a> <a href="/wiki/Dan_Halutz" title="Dan Halutz">Dan Halutz</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup> and calls for resignations of many cabinet-members including Prime-Minister Ehud Olmert following publication of the <a href="/wiki/Winograd_Commission" title="Winograd Commission">Winograd Commission</a>'s findings.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup> The Winograd report severely criticized Olmert, accusing him of a "severe failure in exercising judgment, responsibility and caution." Lebanese Prime Minister Fouad Siniora criticized the Winograd report for failing to report on the full destruction dealt to Lebanon by the brief July War of 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the war, the Lebanese Army deployed 15,000 soldiers, backed by a UNIFIL force of 12,000, deployed South of the <a href="/wiki/Litani_River" title="Litani River">Litani River</a> to replace Hezbollah, although the Lebanese government said that it cannot and will not disarm Hezbollah by force. On 7 February 2010, the Lebanese Army fired at an Israeli bulldozer on the border, and Israeli forces returned fire. There were no reported casualties. Lebanon claimed that the bulldozer had crossed the border and entered Lebanese territory. On 21 February 2007, <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Army">Lebanese Army</a> troops fired at an Israeli UAV over <a href="/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon" title="Tyre, Lebanon">Tyre</a> with small arms, causing no damage.<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 June 2007, UN Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-Moon" class="mw-redirect" title="Ban Ki-Moon">Ban Ki-Moon</a>'s fourth report on the implementation of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1701" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1701">Security Council Resolution 1701</a> fingered Israel, Lebanon and Hezbollah for violating the ceasefire, but called the firing of rockets into Israel by unknown elements "the most serious breach of the cessation of hostilities since the end of the war." The report commended Israel on its restraint following this attack, and commended Lebanon for its continued efforts to disarm armed groups. It further stated that in spite of "flexibility by Israel beyond the framework of UNSC-Resolution 1701, implementation of the resolution's humanitarian aspects has not yet been possible."<sup id="cite_ref-forthReportOfTheSecretaryGeneral_390-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forthReportOfTheSecretaryGeneral-390">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 12 February 2008, <a href="/wiki/Imad_Mugniyah" class="mw-redirect" title="Imad Mugniyah">Imad Mugniyah</a>, the head of Hezbollah's military wing, was assassinated by a car bomb in Damascus.<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">&#91;391&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">Mossad</a>, Israel's intelligence agency, was widely believed to be behind the assassination. Although Israel officially denied involvement, Mugniyah had been the target of previous Mossad assassination attempts.<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">&#91;392&#93;</a></sup> Israel considered Mugniyah a "significant force behind actions against Israel".<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">&#91;393&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 July 2009, an explosion in <a href="/wiki/Khirbat_Silim" class="mw-redirect" title="Khirbat Silim">Khirbat Silim</a>, a Lebanese village near the Lebanon-Israel border, killed eight Hezbollah militants. Israel and the United Nations stated that the explosion was a hidden Hezbollah weapons cache, and condemned Hezbollah for violating Resolution 1701. The Lebanese government stated that the explosion was caused by IDF munitions left following the 2006 war.<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">&#91;394&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup> Hezbollah blamed the explosion on leftover shells that had been collected following Israel's withdrawal from Lebanon in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup> A Kuwaiti newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/Al-Seyassah" title="Al-Seyassah">al-Seyassah</a></i>, reported that the ammunition warehouse stored <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemical weapons">chemical weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 August 2009, the IDF published a video it said showed villagers from <a href="/wiki/Marwakhin" class="mw-redirect" title="Marwakhin">Marwakhin</a>, a village in Southern Lebanon, "forcefully resisting" efforts by Hezbollah militants to store weapons in their village.<sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-398">&#91;398&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 4 November 2009 <a href="/wiki/Israeli_navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli navy">Israeli navy</a> <a href="/wiki/Commando" title="Commando">commandos</a> of <a href="/wiki/Shayetet_13" title="Shayetet 13">Shayetet 13</a> boarded the ship <a href="/wiki/MV_Francop" title="MV Francop">MV&#160;<i>Francop</i></a> in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> and seized 500 tons of Iranian armaments disguised as civilian cargo. Israel said the weapons were bound for Hezbollah and originated from Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">&#91;399&#93;</a></sup> Hezbollah disavowed any connection to the contraband and accused Israel of "piracy."<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">&#91;400&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Lebanese Army in May 2010 it fired <a href="/wiki/Anti-aircraft_artillery" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-aircraft artillery">anti-aircraft artillery</a> at two Israeli jets over Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, French UNIFIL forces warned that they could in the future attack Israeli jets with anti-aircraft batteries if Israel continued its overflights of Lebanese airspace.<sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-402">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 4 August 2010, <a href="/wiki/2010_Israel%E2%80%93Lebanon_border_clash" title="2010 Israel–Lebanon border clash">a clash on the border</a> occurred when the Israel military tried to remove a tree from between the border and the border fence on Israeli territory. According to the Israelis, the tree was blocking the view of one of their video cameras at the border. The Lebanese army fired at the Israeli forces and there was a clash for a few hours. In the ensuing clash, one Israeli soldier died as well as two Lebanese soldiers and one Lebanese journalist. There were also a number of injured military soldiers and civilians on both sides including Lebanese journalists.<sup id="cite_ref-403" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-403">&#91;403&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prisoner_swap">Prisoner swap</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2008_Israel%E2%80%93Hezbollah_prisoner_exchange" title="2008 Israel–Hezbollah prisoner exchange">2008 Israel–Hezbollah prisoner exchange</a></div>
<p>On Wednesday 16 July 2008, in accordance with the mandates of <a href="/wiki/Resolution_1701" class="mw-redirect" title="Resolution 1701">Resolution 1701</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> transferred the coffins of captured Israeli soldiers,<sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-404">&#91;404&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Goldwasser" title="Ehud Goldwasser">Ehud Goldwasser</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eldad_Regev" title="Eldad Regev">Eldad Regev</a>, in exchange for incarcerated <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Front" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestine Liberation Front">Palestine Liberation Front</a> militant <a href="/wiki/Samir_Kuntar" title="Samir Kuntar">Samir Kuntar</a>, four Hezbollah militants captured by Israel during the war, and bodies of about 200 other Lebanese and Palestinian militants held by Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz_14_August_2008_405-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz_14_August_2008-405">&#91;405&#93;</a></sup> Until that time, Hezbollah had provide no information on Goldwasser and Regev's condition and disallowed the Red Cross from visiting them.<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz_14_August_2008_405-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz_14_August_2008-405">&#91;405&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_film">In film</span></h3>
<p>The 2006 Lebanon War is the subject of two feature length films, both of which were screened at the <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_at_the_2008_Sundance_Film_Festival" title="List of films at the 2008 Sundance Film Festival">2008 Sundance Film Festival</a>. They are <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Aractingi" title="Philippe Aractingi">Philippe Aractingi</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Under_the_Bombs" title="Under the Bombs">Under the Bombs</a></i> (2007) and Guy Nattiv and Erez Tadmor's <i><a href="/wiki/Strangers_(2007_Israeli_film)" title="Strangers (2007 Israeli film)">Strangers</a></i> (2007).<sup id="cite_ref-406" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-406">&#91;406&#93;</a></sup> Israeli soldier and documentary filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Yariv_Mozer" title="Yariv Mozer">Yariv Mozer</a> also wrote, directed and filmed the autobiographical "My First War" based on his experiences in the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-407" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-407">&#91;407&#93;</a></sup> The conflict was also the subject of an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Anthony_Bourdain:_No_Reservations" title="Anthony Bourdain: No Reservations">Anthony Bourdain: No Reservations</a></i>, which was nominated for an Emmy Award for Outstanding Informational Programming in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-408">&#91;408&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A collective of Lebanese filmmakers produced during and in the immediate aftermath of the war some twenty short videos that were released as <i>Videos Under Siege</i> and presented in numerous festivals including the <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Film_Festival" title="Dubai International Film Festival">Dubai International Film Festival</a>. The directors involved included <a href="/wiki/Akram_Zaatari" title="Akram Zaatari">Akram Zaatari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khalil_Joreige" title="Khalil Joreige">Khalil Joreige</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joana_Hadjithomas" title="Joana Hadjithomas">Joana Hadjithomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danielle_Arbid" title="Danielle Arbid">Danielle Arbid</a>, Tina Baz, <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Buchakjian" title="Gregory Buchakjian">Gregory Buchakjian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghassan_Salhab" title="Ghassan Salhab">Ghassan Salhab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rania_Stephan" title="Rania Stephan">Rania Stephan</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">&#91;409&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
